  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_02cffc4d-4a6f-4569-a6d2-b9ca59f8bd38'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer644688894445728766"><i>Some kisses come at a price.</i><br/><br/>War has begun. Arin is in the thick of it with untrustworthy new allies and the empire as his enemy. Though he has convinced himself that he no longer loves Kestrel, Arin hasn’t forgotten her, or how she became exactly the kind of person he has always despised.   <span id="freeText644688894445728766" style="display:none"><i>Some kisses come at a price.</i><br /><br />War has begun. Arin is in the thick of it with untrustworthy new allies and the empire as his enemy. Though he has convinced himself that he no longer loves Kestrel, Arin hasn’t forgotten her, or how she became exactly the kind of person he has always despised. She cared more for the empire than she did for the lives of innocent people—and certainly more than she did for him.<br /><br />At least, that’s what he thinks.<br /><br />In the frozen north, Kestrel is a prisoner in a brutal work camp. As she searches desperately for a way to escape, she wishes Arin could know what she sacrificed for him. She wishes she could make the empire pay for what they’ve done to her.<br /><br />But no one gets what they want just by wishing.<br /><br />As the war intensifies, both Kestrel and Arin discover that the world is changing. The East is pitted against the West, and they are caught in between. With so much to lose, can anybody really win?</span>

      $('edition_30816686').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_30816686').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_30816686').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_30816686').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {

The new covers will be for the paperbacks. The hardbacks<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The publisher decided to keep the old cover (with the red dress) for the third hardback book. The new covers will be for the paperbacks. The hardbacks will match each other. So will the paperbacks.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1130012084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130012084" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1130012084?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130012084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6220718439606700263"><blockquote>
  <i>No battle is won without a good gamble.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>This series has come a long way from its tame romantic beginnings in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_' title='The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winner's Curse</a></b>. The final installment finishes the series on an emotional, action-packed high, weaving in more game, winning and gambling metaphors to add to the running theme.<br/><br/>A couple of years ago, I was disappointed with the much-loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_' title='The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winner's Curse</a>. The author had a good writing style that engaged the reader, but it was so tame! So much romance dampening the secrets, reveng</span>
  <span id="freeText6220718439606700263" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>No battle is won without a good gamble.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>This series has come a long way from its tame romantic beginnings in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a></b>. The final installment finishes the series on an emotional, action-packed high, weaving in more game, winning and gambling metaphors to add to the running theme.<br /><br />A couple of years ago, I was disappointed with the much-loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a>. The author had a good writing style that engaged the reader, but it was so tame! So much romance dampening the secrets, revenge and betrayals. However, I was so happy I gave in and tried <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443207.The_Winner_s_Crime__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___2_" title="The Winner's Crime (The Winner's Trilogy, #2) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Crime</a>, a far more well-written, well-developed book with a fantastic story and just enough romance.<br /><br />This book, though, is a <b>near perfect ending</b>. From start to finish, it's a nasty, bloodthirsty tale with no more niceties. Hands get dirty, shit goes down, and people surprise you. There's a constant pull of action and horror, forcing you to read "just one more chapter" until suddenly you've reached the end. <br /><br />Combine that with some <b>clever storytelling</b> and <b>intricate relationships</b>, and you have one hell of a good book.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>But nothing is ever simple between the gods, and the stories of the gods of war and games were many...</i>
</blockquote><br />Each page flows into the next with perfect dialogue and tension. Rutkoski uses quickly changing perspectives in the most dramatic scenes, setting up a cliffhanger with Kestrel before jumping to Arin and leaving you desperate to know more. This has failed in other books, but the author manages it expertly here. <br /><br />Because of this, the big battle scene is perfectly told, with plenty of heart-stopping moments.<br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443235.The_Winner_s_Kiss__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___3_" title="The Winner's Kiss (The Winner's Trilogy, #3) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Kiss</a>, the romance is more mature. Kestrel and Arin are no longer simply blushing teens from different sides of the track. They've been through so much, grown as characters, and I think this final chapter of their relationship will satisfy romantics and non-romantics alike.<br /><br />More importantly, Rutkoski doesn't neglect secondary characters and the protagonists' relationship with them. Special attention is given to Kestrel, her father and the complex dynamics between them, as well as the comical relationship between Arin and Roshar that involves a lot of banter and bickering.<br /><br /><b>Entertaining, dark, and completely worth pushing through the first book for.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6220718439606700263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1114785908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114785908" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1114785908?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=cool-author">cool-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=macmillan">macmillan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=beautiful-prose">beautiful-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=sexy-times">sexy-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=alternating-povs">alternating-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=awesome">awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=pure-win">pure-win</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=oh-yeah-baby">oh-yeah-baby</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114785908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12541780041822261455">Final books are hard. Readers dive in with so many expectations, hopes and fears, and let's not forget the ships. I suspect it must be at least a little daunting for an author to want to give their readers everything and stay true to their story. Friends, for me, Marie Rutkoski has done just that. This story has taken me on a remarkable journey, capturing my heart and and melting my emotions in one fell swoop. <br/><br/><i>The Winner's Kiss</i> is a perfect conclusion to an expertly crafted series. And as always</span>
  <span id="freeText12541780041822261455" style="display:none">Final books are hard. Readers dive in with so many expectations, hopes and fears, and let's not forget the ships. I suspect it must be at least a little daunting for an author to want to give their readers everything and stay true to their story. Friends, for me, Marie Rutkoski has done just that. This story has taken me on a remarkable journey, capturing my heart and and melting my emotions in one fell swoop. <br><br><i>The Winner's Kiss</i> is a perfect conclusion to an expertly crafted series. And as always there are many familiar reasons to love the final installment as much as its predecessors while containing quite a few twists that kept me anticipating the turn of each page. Our protagonists, Kestrel and Arin, experience a lot of growth as previous choices finally reach shocking, climatic consequences, many of which I was unsure how they'd move past. I definitely didn't expect the changes Kestrel underwent; she is both the same and vastly different, exploring physical and mental strength of female characters. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>You don't need to be gifted with a blade. You are your own best weapon.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The unpredictability of this novel is <i>its</i> greatest weapon as Rutkoski clearly shows she's not afraid to make you beg for your favorites' survival. She's heartlessly brilliant like that. <br><br>What I didn't expect was how much I enjoyed Roshar's character. I give his sarcastic, witty remarks an A++ and loved how he reminded me of a rougher version of Sturmhond from The Grisha series. It was smart for him to have as much page time as he did since <i>The Winner's Kiss</i> contains romantic tension to the max with a few scenes causing me utter desperation—moments where I was throwing buckets of water out of my ship, lest it sink, screaming "Noooooooooo!" fiercely at my ceiling. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453526126ra/17837669.gif" alt=" photo IMG_0687_zpsu4rvftol.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I still admire the writing and how it manages to convey so much more than is actually written. It's made me re-think my stance on 3rd person narration, usually my least favorite. But the fact that I, too, now feel as though I can translate Kestrel and Arin's Epic Starring Contests, Roshar and Arin's Bromatic Body Language among a host of other tells, just goes to show you the quality of writing. No words are wasted, and always feel so carefully deliberate while still maintaining its raw honesty. <br><br>Perhaps what <i>The Winner's Kiss</i> succeeds at the most is its ability to straddle that fine line between a character driven and plot driven novel. Neither side took over the other, out-shining or lacking in development. The relationships were given the proper amount of time and dignity. Not only is there a focus on Kestrel and Arin's, but also of another that's made very clear it's just as important, and maybe even more so. And, yes, in case you were wondering, this book does indeed pass the Bechdel test, something which I'm always pleased to see in a YA novel. <br><br>The plot was excellent. Surprisingly detailed battle scenes, strategies and political maneuvers are at the front without making my eyes glaze over with confusion. And I loved that Arin's cultural religious beliefs along side Kestrel's disbelief was handled with a great amount of respect and love. It really highlighted an ongoing theme of tolerance and respect of others' differences, and that is so incredibly relevant. And, of course, I really enjoyed how the novel began and ended with A Winner's Curse, bringing the entire series full circle. Nice touch. <br><br>I am fiercely in love with all things Kestrel and Arin. Their relationship struggle in the novel was so real. Finally a YA book where it's not the fantasy world keeping them apart, but actual real relationship bumps that plagues us all: break down of communication, acknowledgements of individual changes and growth, trust issues, accepting faults along with strengths, understanding personal struggles, guilt of hurting the one you love the most, forgiveness, and above all, mutual respect. <br><br>Favorite quote: <br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"He changed us both." She seemed to struggle for words. "I think of you, all that you lost, who you were, what you were forced to be, and might have been, and I—I have become this, this <i>person</i>, unable to—"<br>She shut her mouth. <br>"Kestrel," he said softly, "I love this person."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>It's sad for me to come to the conclusion of a favorite series, one that I never expected to adore so much. But I loved every minute of this ride and can't wait to revisit. <br><br>Highly recommending. <br><br>Excellent series is excellent. <br><br><i>An ARC was provided by the publisher. No monies or favors were exchanged.</i><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://Cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12541780041822261455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1134919974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1134919974" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1134919974?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134919974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5517079174078010235"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski' title='Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>Marie Rutkoski</a> isn't an ordinary author.<br/><b>She's an artist.</b><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Later, Kestrel wished she had spoken then, that no time had been lost. She wished that she’d had the courage that very moment to tell Arin what she’d finally known to be true: that she loved him with the whole of her heart.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443235.The_Winner_s_Kiss__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___3_' title='The Winner's Kiss (The Winner's Trilogy, #3) by Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winner's Kiss</a> isn't an ordinary book.<br/>It's a poem. A sad melody. The blood that pumps in your veins. The air that ruffles your hair.<br/>It's a promise. A promise of love lost and found.<br/><b>It is beauty, in its pu</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5517079174078010235" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski" title="Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Rutkoski</a> isn't an ordinary author.<br><b>She's an artist.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Later, Kestrel wished she had spoken then, that no time had been lost. She wished that she’d had the courage that very moment to tell Arin what she’d finally known to be true: that she loved him with the whole of her heart.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443235.The_Winner_s_Kiss__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___3_" title="The Winner's Kiss (The Winner's Trilogy, #3) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Kiss</a> isn't an ordinary book.<br>It's a poem. A sad melody. The blood that pumps in your veins. The air that ruffles your hair.<br>It's a promise. A promise of love lost and found.<br><b>It is beauty, in its purest and most radiant form.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459538863ra/18624339.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The tale of two enemies that fell in love, lied, schemed and betrayed each other continues, sweeping everything in its path. Arin tries to win a war that seems like a lost cause, Kestrel pays the price of her mistakes. Arin wants to forget her, Kestrel tries to forgive him. They're hurt and angry, desperate and hopeful, ready to gamble one last time, to find out whether they're blessed or cursed. To find out whether they can handle the truth.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Every chip of her being slid into place, into the image of a lost world. The boy discovering it. The girl who sees it spark and flare, and understands, now, what she feels. She realizes that she has felt this for a long time.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Do you know the feeling when you love a book so much that the mere thought of it makes your chest swell and your heart ache and your eyes water? It's the most satisfying feeling in the world. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski" title="Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Rutkoski</a> managed to compose a <b>tale of war and love with threads of sadness, hope and despair, </b>all of them at the same time. Her writing is <b>lyrical. Expressive. </b>You can taste it in your tongue. You can travel into faraway lands, smell the gunpowder, shiver under the rain. Her descriptions, her battle plans, her military strategies, everything is crafted so masterly that you can't help but bow to her brilliant mind and her brilliant pen. She has the power to shatter your heart and then mend it, and repeat the same process until you don't know what's left of you to give but you give it nonetheless. She <i>is</i> magic.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459542454ra/18624707.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He hadn't been blessed by the god of death.<br>Arin was the god of death.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>God of death or god of lies, Arin is a character you can't help but love deeply. He's changed, he doesn't regret the blood he's shed, he's cunning and manipulative, but he's also afraid. He blames himself for every misfortune that's ever happened to the people he cares about but he loves fiercely and expects nothing in return. In this book his patience and his thoughtfulness made me weep several times. But Kestrel's trials also bought me tears. She had been strong for so long that she finally gave up, and the result was <b>gut-wrenching</b>. All she ever wanted has her father to love her for who she is, she wanted his approval and his acceptance and all she got was pain and betrayal. She was afraid to open up her heart again, and Arin posed the most imminent danger. <b>Her pride, her wit and her fire make her one of the best female heroines an author has ever created.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“She looked into the shadowed corners of the room. Talking with him was like having a flower unfold inside her chest, then close up tight. Creep open. Collapse in on itself.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>In the final book of this trilogy, Arin and Kestrel got to know each other and fall in love from the start and this time, there were no lies and deception but bluntness and honesty. And trust. Roshar's part managed to break the tension and offer lighthearted moments of laughter, a great addition to help me breathe. Because I drowned in a sea of bittersweet, agonizing emotions and I was overwhelmed by a longing and a desire so palpable that felt like they were my own. But Marie didn't focus only on romantic love. There was also the family love, a bond that seemed broken and even though you were angry, deep down you wanted it to survive.<br><br>And now that this magnificent series has ended, I don't want to say goodbye. Instead, I'll say thank you. <b>Thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski" title="Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Rutkoski</a>. For Arin and Kestrel. For this wonderful ending. For everything.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443884449ra/16425875.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Come closer, and I will tell you."<br>But he forgot. He kissed her, and became lost in the exquisite sensation of his skin becoming too tight for his body. He murmured other things instead. A secret, a want, a promise. A story, in its own way.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="5517079174078010235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1347979463" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1347979463" />
    <a title="Dorreh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh"><img alt="Dorreh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565727363p2/22599584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1347979463?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorreh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorreh" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh">Dorreh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347979463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5007798579368023012">"He didn’t smile. He cupped her face with both hands. An emotion tugged at his expression, a dark awe, the kind saved for a wild storm that rends the sky but doesn’t ravage your existence, doesn’t destroy every thing you love. The one that lets you feel saved"<br/><br/>I finally finished this series! YAY!!!!<br/><br/>I promised myself no more reading until after my basic science exam, but I broke it. Shame on me!<br/><br/>I have this hollow feeling after reading this book, I loved it and all, but the ending left me kind of d</span>
  <span id="freeText5007798579368023012" style="display:none">"He didn’t smile. He cupped her face with both hands. An emotion tugged at his expression, a dark awe, the kind saved for a wild storm that rends the sky but doesn’t ravage your existence, doesn’t destroy every thing you love. The one that lets you feel saved"<br /><br />I finally finished this series! YAY!!!!<br /><br />I promised myself no more reading until after my basic science exam, but I broke it. Shame on me!<br /><br />I have this hollow feeling after reading this book, I loved it and all, but the ending left me kind of devastated. I honestly can't tell if it was because I wasn't ready to accept this series came to an end, or because Ive been in a weird mood these past few days. This book felt like nostalgia, a melancholic touch of vague feelings. Maybe better said a kind of chilly dejavú. <br /><br />"She pressed her face into the pillow. His scent was there. She was stupid to have come, yet didn’t have the strength to leave.<br />The ghost of him between the sheets. The shadow of her old self curled into the shadow of him."<br /><br />This was my favorite part, truly. It was so beautiful, I wanted to curl onto myself with raw emotion. It was so intimate, a kind of intimacy born of desperation and need unfulfilled. An illusion of intimacy per day. <br />At the begging I was so happy and overwhelmed with joy about the fact that instead of a pity party like I had expected, Krestel picks herself up no matter how many times she falls, I was further exhilarated when she lost all memory of Arin. It was a second chance for them to fall in love, and for me to love them all over again. For the first half of the book, the story is amazing, its unique, it's emotionally plundering, a true roller coaster. The typical after becoming a couple drama that usually is the main staple of the final installment in trilogies was absent. BUT, somewhere along the way, around the second half of the book I felt like I was reading a completely different book. Maybe I'm mistaken, but it felt like the writing style somehow changed, as if the author were someone else entirely. The characters behavior, the fast pace and plotting, everything was the same yet different. At some point the book had taken on a poetic stance. Krestel went from clever and witty to, I don't know, somehow docile? It wasn't bad, it was just different.<br /><br />"Kestrel felt a slow, slight throb, a shimmer in the blood. She knew it well.<br />Her worst trait. Her best trait.<br />The desire to come out on top, to set her opponent under her thumb.<br />A streak of pride. Her mind ringed with hungry rows of foxlike teeth."<br /><br />This is why I love Krestel, why she became a YA protagonist favorite. I love ambition, and more than that I love ordinary people who strive for their ambitions, they don't whine and ask it handed to them on a silver platter.<br /><br />I can't really word properly how I felt, and maybe it's just me, but it just felt changed. I'm not complaining, or okay, yes I am, maybe just a little. I loved the winners crime so much, that honestly the second half of this book disappointed me a little. The storyline ended amazingly, I couldn't even go near predicting how things would end. It was beautiful and touching, a perfect ending to an amazing series. I guess it's just the mindset that you read something in that determines how great you feel. <br /><br />Overall this book was an emotional and thrilling, imaginative, and creatively expressed. It had everything a YA novel needs. It was a easy flowing book, and was powerful in terms of literary writing. It also like I mentioned earlier, had a poetic drift to it. Maybe it was perhaps that both the protagonists were artists in their own way. One a creator of music and the other a player of instruments. I felt the softness to the souls that were created on these fictional characters, and that was beautiful. If I have the time to reread a series, I'd probably choose this one again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5007798579368023012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText52483497945976257" style="display:none">Reread and man oh man, this story still has so much soul, depth and authenticity that only gets richer with each reread. <br />It’s not a story that I’ll ever tire off. I’m in love! <br /><br />————————————<br /><br /><b>Original review.</b><br />"You don’t need to be gifted with a blade. You are your own best weapon."<br /><br />Well, shit. This book!!!! My heart feel so heavy right now. I'm so sad that it's over! <br /><br />The Winner's Kiss was absolute perfection for me, start to finish. Every page. My mind is all over the place at the moment, and I cannot find the words to declare my love for this trilogy or write a comprehensive review for it. <br /><br />The things is, I didn't even expect it to become one of my favourite trilogies. The first book lacked a lot of things for me, in terms of world building and character explorations. Nevertheless, I enjoyed it, but, didn't love it. However, the second and third instalments, improved drastically and beautifully, and my heart is bursting with love for these books right now. <br /><br />Marie Rutkoski took her sweet time and gave every character, every detail, every element to this story its due right. I could't help but fall in love with him. <br /><br />The characters and the story is something that has now embedded itself into my heart. I had the best time reading it and I'm already looking forward to the day I decide to reread them.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2316819461" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2316819461" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2316819461?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=greco-roman">greco-roman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2316819461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer219950148459954041"><b>“You don't need to be gifted with a blade. You are your own best weapon.”</b><br/><br/><i>*Please note that there are spoilers from the Winner’s Curse and the Winner’s Crime, as well as some minor ones from the Winner’s Kiss. So, if you haven’t read these, proceed at your own risk.*</i> (aka: don’t @ me in the comments for spoilers!)<br/><br/>This was another buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2551594955' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laura</a>, of course (OMG this is like our fourth by now. Go us!). AND NYAH NYAH NYAH! I’M WINNING AGAIN! MUAHAHAHAHA! ;)<br/><br/>The roles have seemingly reversed in</span>
  <span id="freeText219950148459954041" style="display:none"><b>“You don't need to be gifted with a blade. You are your own best weapon.”</b><br /><br /><i>*Please note that there are spoilers from the Winner’s Curse and the Winner’s Crime, as well as some minor ones from the Winner’s Kiss. So, if you haven’t read these, proceed at your own risk.*</i> (aka: don’t @ me in the comments for spoilers!)<br /><br />This was another buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2551594955" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura</a>, of course (OMG this is like our fourth by now. Go us!). AND NYAH NYAH NYAH! I’M WINNING AGAIN! MUAHAHAHAHA! ;)<br /><br />The roles have seemingly reversed in this instalment of the Winner’s trilogy. <b>Arin</b> is now led by the <b>god of Death</b>, killing anything that comes across his path or gets in his way to seek revenge against the Valorians. He wants to destroy all those who have wronged his family and his people, and he doesn’t care what he has to do in order to accomplish it. <b>Kestrel</b>, on the other hand, is now <b>a slave</b> in a work camp, drugged to the point where she no longer knows who she even is anymore. Everything that made Kestrel the amazing protagonist that she is…<i>no longer exists</i>. She and Arin finally have common ground in the sense that they both have <i>physical and mental scars</i> that will haunt them until they find a way to overcome their inner demons. <br /><br />This instalment was great, albeit rather dark, in comparison with the past two. Yet, it simultaneously came across as a light <i>rom-com</i> because <b>the first 75%</b> of this novel revolves around Arin and Kestrel’s <b>romance</b>, making the reader <i>forget about the war</i> that they were supposedly fighting in the first place. <br /><br />I could barely even recognise Kestrel anymore because she’s essentially a shell of the person that she once was. <b>Amnesia</b> is always a very difficult trope to tackle – and Rutkoski seems to have a penchant for filling her books with <b>an abundance of tropes</b> from <i>slavery</i> in book one, <i>political intrigue</i> in book two and <i>memory loss</i> in book three – and I think that it wasn’t handled very well. Having taken a few university-level classes in Psychology, I know that amnesia is sometimes <b>a defence mechanism for traumatic events</b>, but that’s not how it’s used here. Rather, a drug is what takes Kestrel’s memory away. And instead of gradually getting her memories back, since her body is no longer addicted to the drug, she remembers inconsequential events at random intervals…and then remembers everything <i>all at once</i>, which defies everything that is known about amnesia. Either your memory slowly returns over an extended period of time, or you never recover it at all. In addition, after everything, Kestrel somehow isn’t suffering from <i>post-traumatic stress</i>??? How???! She was betrayed by her father, a man that she trusted to protect her above all else, and he essentially threw her to the wolves, by sending her to a certain death. The most we get is her crying on Arin’s shoulder as he promises to love her (which was <i>SUCH</i> a sweet moment). <br /><br /><b>Kestrel:</b> <i>“I want better choices.”</i><br /><b>Arin:</b> <i>“Then we must make a world that has them.”</i><br /><br />On a more positive note, I did <i>FINALLY</i> end up enjoying the <b>romance</b> between Arin and Kestrel, although I am still not certain why Arin fell in love with her, but I already covered that in a previous review. I don’t really want to go over it again, haha. Ultimately, I found Arin’s <i>complete and utter devotion</i> to Kestrel to be rather sweet in this instalment, and I liked that Kestrel didn’t allow her insecurities, left behind from her father’s abandonment, to hinder her from finally coming clean to Arin about <i>how she really feels</i> about him. They’re not an all-time favourite ship of mine by any means, but at least, I can somewhat appreciate it now.<br /><br /><b>Roshar and Arin, the tiger</b>, were absolute delights, who made me smile every time that they appeared on the page. &lt;3 It was sad to see Roshar hiding his true feelings behind his bravado, but we did get to see how genuinely he cares for Arin…his friend. Also, I lived for every moment when he complained that Kestrel “murders [him]” at every game, even asking Arin if she has anything that she’s <i>NOT</i> good at! Ahhhh…how I love him! :D Considering that <b>Verex</b> was my favourite character in the previous instalment, I was extremely disappointed that we only saw him <b>a total of three times</b> in this entire novel. As the son of the Emperor, he could’ve had a much more integral role. This was an opportunity that Rotkoski definitely <i>squandered</i>.<br /><br />Two of my biggest complaints about this trilogy have been <b>the fantasy elements and the world building</b>. Well, the world building remained the same…meaning, that there still wasn’t any. I don’t think that <i>the inclusion of maps</i> counts as world building, and that’s basically all we get. In regards to fantasy elements, a <b>strange mythology</b> came out of nowhere. Suddenly, Arin is being advised constantly by the god of Death, despite not having done so in the past two books, and I’m very confused as to why Rutkoski decided to include this. I had accepted that this was more of an alternate history, until she threw this unexplained mythology upon me. Needless to say, I’m <i>NOT A FAN</i> of it. And this is coming from a person who lives and breathes mythology, ugh. <br /><br />As always, Rotkoski’s <b>addicting writing style</b> hooked me in from beginning to end, but it still wasn’t able to distract me from the fact that there was basically <b>no plot</b>. Everything of note occurred during <b>the last 25%</b> of the novel, and only then did Kestrel really use her <b>strategic sense</b> that we love. As such, I found the ending to be rather <i>anticlimactic</i>. In addition, after all of the angst that goes on between Kestrel and her father, nothing is really resolved. In all actuality, <i>nothing is really resolved</i> because Rutkoski decided to leave us with an open ending, which I wasn’t a fan of. What happens to them??? What happens to the world??? <i>I NEED ANSWERS!</i><br /><br />Despite all of these criticisms, I did <i>really enjoy</i> this novel, but as more and more time passed after having completed it, I realised that I had so many complaints that I needed to address. Thus, this is more of a <b>3.5-star rating</b>. This is by no means, a poor book, but as I’m typing out this review, I’m starting to realise that once it’s finished and the story sinks in, there’s more bad than good. I’d classify it as a <i>guilty pleasure YA read</i>, that doesn’t necessarily have the substance of a Laini Taylor or Leigh Bardugo book, for example. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ Sorry, if I’m dissing your favourite series… :( <br /><br /><b>Kestrel</b> will always stay with me as a <b>loveable protagonist</b>, but I’m kind of disappointed that this author hasn’t written a lot more books. I want more!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="219950148459954041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1556713428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556713428" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1556713428?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408858745" href="/book/show/25526307-the-winner-s-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=published-2016">published-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1556713428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4419716139713740547"><blockquote><i>Are you really a boy, like Xash says?</i> the god asked Arin. <i>You’ve been mine for twenty years. I raised you.</i><br/>The Valorian signed the scrap of paper.<br/><i>Cared for you.</i><br/>The message was rolled, sealed, and pushed into a tiny leather tube.<br/><i>Watched over you when you thought you were alone.</i><br/>The captain tied the tube to hawk’s leg. The bird was too large to be a kestrel. It didn’t have a kestrel’s markings. It cocked its head, turning its glass-bead eyes on Arin.<br/><i>No, not a boy. A man made in my image…one who know</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4419716139713740547" style="display:none"><blockquote><i>Are you really a boy, like Xash says?</i> the god asked Arin. <i>You’ve been mine for twenty years. I raised you.</i><br />The Valorian signed the scrap of paper.<br /><i>Cared for you.</i><br />The message was rolled, sealed, and pushed into a tiny leather tube.<br /><i>Watched over you when you thought you were alone.</i><br />The captain tied the tube to hawk’s leg. The bird was too large to be a kestrel. It didn’t have a kestrel’s markings. It cocked its head, turning its glass-bead eyes on Arin.<br /><i>No, not a boy. A man made in my image…one who knows he can’t afford to be seen as weak.</i><br />The hawk launched into the sky.<br /><i>You’re mine, Arin. You know what you must do.</i><br />Arin cut the Valorian’s throat.</blockquote> <br /><b>I’m speechless.<br /><br />This book was the perfect ending to one of my all-time favourite series.</b> I can't believe it's over. But it was a beautiful ride, Marie Rutkoski, a truly beautiful ride.<br /><br />Let’s do some reminiscing. When I first picked up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a> my expectations were pretty low. Books with girls in dresses on the cover? Focused primarily on romance? Not really my thing. However, as soon as I started the novel two things became very clear.<br /><br />1)	The writing was STUNNING.<br />2)	I loved the female protagonist, Kestrel.<br /><br />As the book went on, these feelings intensified and I found myself drawn to this story of star-crossed lovers despite my aversion towards romance and books that don’t contain enough world-building. <b>So I ended up really liking the first book in this series, but I wasn’t in love with it yet.</b><br /><br />Then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443207.The_Winner_s_Crime__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___2_" title="The Winner's Crime (The Winner's Trilogy, #2) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Crime</a> came along (click <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114215328?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> here for my review) and <b>I was blown out of the water</b>. It was vastly different form <i>The Winner’s Curse</i>, so different in fact, that I even hesitate to compare the two because they attempted such different things, elicited such different emotions. But I adored it.<br /><br />And then we have this book. Was it my favourite? Maybe. Probably.<b><i> The Winner’s Kiss</i> has a maturity and depth that goes beyond the other two. It is more bloody and bloodthristy, more raw and graphic. This final instalment in the series has everything you could hope for: beautiful writing, fleshed-out, flawed characters, better world-building, fast-paced action, tons of emotion, character development, the list goes on.</b> <br /><br />I fear I will never be able to make this book justice, so I’m going to try and just pick out a few things I absolutely loved. <br /><br />First let’s start with what is probably my favourite thing about the series. Kestrel. As Risha put it so wisely<br /><blockquote>You don't need to be gifted with a blade. You are your own best weapon.</blockquote> <br />Yes, that indeed she is. Kestrel is my favourite type of character: intelligent, brave, rational, strong, <b>a tactician</b>. Authors like writing these kinds of characters, I see them often. However, it’s quite rare that I see them done well. If they are well-done, the outcome is glorious. The results are the Light Yagami’s, Lelouche vi Britannia’s and Kelsier’s of the world. But more often than not, this isn’t the case because the writer forgets a fundamental rule: show, don’t tell. We might end up with books where the narration keeps going on about how great a character is without showing anything or we are told through the thoughts of other characters or dialogue. But Marie Rutkoski is better than that. <b>We can tell Kestrel is intelligent and tactically gifted, not only through other people’s thoughts, but through her actions. In this book, she did things that surprised me, awed me, made me gasp for air. She was EVERYTHING. Absolutely fabulous.</b><br /><br />Then we have Arin. I admit, I wasn’t the biggest Arin fan in the first two books. I liked him and Kestrel as a couple, but him as a character I found rather unimpressive. He dulled next to Kestrel. <b>Not so in this book. He really grew on me and became strong and determined, gifted in his own right.</b> His utter devotion to Kestrel was palpable and I loved to see how vulnerable it made him, how it cracked open his veneer of composure and strength. <br /><br />Both Arin and Kestrel are deeply flawed characters that had difficult choices to make, choices that can’t always be considered honourable. There are times were the author makes you question the characters’ morality and with it your own beliefs of what is right and wrong. <b>Nothing is simple in war.</b> <br /><br />I also loved the other relationships in the book, particularly <b>the friendship between Arin and Roshar</b>. It was both a heartwarmingly deep connection, but also provided much needed comic relief. <br /><blockquote>Roshar lay on his back, the dip of his neck bolstered by a tied bedroll. He smoked.<br />“I’ve been thinking.”<br />“Dear gods.”<br />“It occurs to me that you have no official rank, and that I, as your prince, might give you one.” He said an eastern word Arin didn’t know. “Well? Will it suit?”<br />“Depends.”<br />“On?”<br />“Whether that word was some horrific insult you’re pretending is an actual military rank.”<br />“How mistrustful! Arin, I have taught you every foul curse I know.”<br />“I’m sure you’ve saved a few, for just such a time.”</blockquote><br />I also loved the exploration of the relationship between Kestrel and her father and Kestrel and Sarsine. <br /><br /><b>The storytelling is exquisite.</b> We have the wonderful metaphoric writing style combined with clever changes in point of view. Marie Rutkoski knows exactly when to switch POV for maximum dramatic effect and how much to tell the reader so he will still be surprised. The plot twists killed me. The battle scenes and war strategies were on point. Also, this was one of the rare books where I really wasn’t sure how it would turn out. The possibility of a main character dying is very real. <b>It made for an anxiety-ridden reading experience.</b><br /><br />This book dealt with many realistic problems that are part of any relationship. Miscommunication, trust issues, growth, guilt, forgiveness. I was rooting for these characters full-heartedly. <br /><br /><b>Overall, I cannot recommend this series enough. It may seem like your typical YA trilogy but it’s honestly one of the best ones I’ve come across and truly special to me. A definite favourite. Highly recommended!</b><br /><br /><i>*I kindly received an e-ARC of this book from Netgalley in exchange for an honest review*</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4419716139713740547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3077125563?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3077125563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2172915696015674874">what a satisfying conclusion to a wonderful series. after the frustration that was <i>'the winners crime,'</i> i had my doubts. but this book reminded me exactly why i love this series. <br/><br/>i love that kestrel is a strong female main character. but it isnt physical strength (which is common in stories set during a war), its mental. we stan a smart and cunning woman. <br/><br/>i love that arin has such a gentleness to him for being an absolute beast. hes ruthless, but hes also tender when it matters. i love that comp</span>
  <span id="freeText2172915696015674874" style="display:none">what a satisfying conclusion to a wonderful series. after the frustration that was <i>'the winners crime,'</i> i had my doubts. but this book reminded me exactly why i love this series. <br /><br />i love that kestrel is a strong female main character. but it isnt physical strength (which is common in stories set during a war), its mental. we stan a smart and cunning woman. <br /><br />i love that arin has such a gentleness to him for being an absolute beast. hes ruthless, but hes also tender when it matters. i love that complexity. <br /><br />but most of all, i love the writing. the writing in this series still continues to surprise me. its rare to find a YA story that has such poetic writing. im used the the simplistic, straight-forward narration often found in this genre, so the elegant prose is such a delight. <br /><br />all i can say is im very happy with how strongly this story ends!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1233645652" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1233645652" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8429172-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595453256p2/8429172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1233645652?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/8429172-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=ebooks-i-own">ebooks-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=amazing-heroines">amazing-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=crying-for-the-rest-of-my-life">crying-for-the-rest-of-my-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=until-the-end-of-the-world">until-the-end-of-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=damn-pretty-covers">damn-pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1233645652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15011255335864450977"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif' width='500' height='245' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b> “I want better choices.”<br/>“Then we must make a world that has them.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>Doesn’t it feel good when you finish a really great book and you just stay still and thank God for what you’ve just read?</i><br/><br/>After this long year of anticipating this book, the only thing I can say is: wow.<br/><br/><u>Remember this review contain untagged spoilers so read at your own risk.</u><br/><br/>Marie’s writing style was as rich and fluid as always and the POVs intricate themselves into something heartbreaking and beautiful. The Winner’s Kiss was f</span>
  <span id="freeText15011255335864450977" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif" width="500" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b> “I want better choices.”<br>“Then we must make a world that has them.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><i>Doesn’t it feel good when you finish a really great book and you just stay still and thank God for what you’ve just read?</i><br><br>After this long year of anticipating this book, the only thing I can say is: wow.<br><br><u>Remember this review contain untagged spoilers so read at your own risk.</u><br><br>Marie’s writing style was as rich and fluid as always and the POVs intricate themselves into something heartbreaking and beautiful. The Winner’s Kiss was fast-paced and it had you on the edge at the end of every single page.<br><br>There were just a very few things I didn’t like so let me tell you about them real quickly.<br><br>•I wasn’t a fan of Kestrel’s father ending up alive. This is me trying to be as neutral as possible: I just don’t see his use. The Herrani will never trust him and he will always be a threat for them, <i>even if he’s held capture.</i> I mean, did they forget it was the general who conquered that country and slaved its people? He will always be a shadow and I don’t see him softening towards Arin and Kestrel’s relationship so, what’s the point? Kestrel would’ve gotten over him if he turned out to be a war casualty. <br><br>•The ending fell short in my opinion-not because it wasn’t satisfying, <i>it was</i>, but it was a bit too happy-ever-after for this bloodthirsty world. I was expecting one last betrayal <i>(from the queen, that’s it. Everything was leading to this banquet at the end and I was expecting them to slaughter Arin and Kestrel or something like that. It would’ve been fucking awful but a really bold move)</i>, if I’m honest.<br><br>•Speaking of that ending-I needed an epilogue. The very ending was cute and amazing but it wasn’t quite enough. It needed this extra something. An epilogue would’ve been a great way to finish this trilogy and give us all a glimpse of their future because… Will Arin rule in Herran? If Verex isn’t taking the Valorian throne, then who is it? Will the eastern queen extend her kingdom to Valoria? There were a lot of questions like these left without an answer and we can only guess what could happen.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407773838ra/10763546.gif" width="500" height="256" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That’s it. That’s all I didn’t like about this book. Now let’s talk about what I absolutely loved.<br><br> <b>Can we talk about how this is the first book I’ve <u>ever</u> read with the amnesia trope that didn’t piss me off?</b> I didn’t think this was possible but damn, I was more than okay with this. <br><br>Kestrel was so hopeless. I mean, I normally don’t like this and how the book can turn into a sob fest but Kestrel had all the right to feel hopeless and sad because she was! She was in such an awful situation, I didn’t know how she could get out. I felt hopeless, too. Kestrel, resourceful, brave, intelligent, fierce and kind Kestrel feeling abandoned, desperate and guilty. If there was someone who had the right to have a pity party, that’d be Kestrel. And yet she was still trying to do something. She was weak, she was human and she gave up but she got back on again and again.<br><br>I just realized how much I love her and how much I appreciate her as a character. She doubt a lot yet she never stopped moving and she grew also so much. Kestrel was never childish sort of character, nor she was your typical YA heroine anyways but the Kestrel you met in book one definitely isn’t this Kestrel. She started questioning her feelings toward Arin when she couldn’t remember what happened and that gave her and me a new perspective and what she felt about her father and her strategies… I think she got so much more cunning and sharp but at the same time she got kinder.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459482514ra/18616304.gif" width="500" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Arin was a tricky character, if you ask me. I really got into him in the last book and so the way he felt about Kestrel broke my heart because he was right to feel that way! I don’t know if I can put myself in his place without seeing things his way. <br><br>He’s got a lot on his plate and the way his god talked to him? I was a bit scared he was going to take Arin’s life at the end. I was way more scared of Arin losing his humanity, to be honest. He also grew a lot: he was less impulsive. It’d be unfair to compare Arin to Kestrel because while Arin suffered a lot while growing up and his people and at risk of sounding insensible, I felt more for Kestrel because I actually saw it happen. So, for me Arin evolved and also his love for Kestrel turned into something way more mature and beautiful. <br><br>His role in the war was really important and I was glad to see more of his mind on action.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459482514ra/18616305.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The way Arin and Kestrel interacted was very different from the previous books due to the fact that there were no more secrets. They were allowed to be playful, cute, in love and honest and that was so good to see.<br><br>Some of their dynamic was heavy but really understandable. They both were afraid and about to die if something went wrong.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“There is a difference between you and me. If I die, you’ll survive. If you die, it will destroy me.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I liked also how others characters jumped into action such as Roshar. I really liked him and the person he pretended to be. He was pompous and I loved it. He was also ruthless but such a cutie.<br><br>Arin’s cousin was unexpected. I didn’t mind her before but I truly liked her in this last book. She was kind and bold.<br><br>Overall this was a very satisfying ending, <i>although I was missing that epilogue</i>. I would highly recommend this trilogy but I never know how to label it. Like, I get it’s dystopia but it has the writing style you find in High Fantasy novels and arg! But it’s so beautiful regardless. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438806486ra/15757186.gif" width="480" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15011255335864450977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1361831551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1361831551" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1361831551?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408858745" href="/book/show/25526307-the-winner-s-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1361831551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13530186045265032713"><b>"Her worst trait. Her best trait.<br/>Her mind ringed with hungry rows of foxlike teeth."</b><br/><br/>I have had to deal with heroines, or called so, of all sorts. The fierce, the whiny, the hotheaded, the softie-and-swoony. The ones who can fight and the ones who cannot, the ones who can think and the ones who cannot; princesses, commoners, magicians, assassins, many, so many of them, and all different one from the other, for better or for worse.<br/>But none, <i>none</i> of them even compare to<b> Kestrel</b>. The one with the cu</span>
  <span id="freeText13530186045265032713" style="display:none"><b>"Her worst trait. Her best trait.<br>Her mind ringed with hungry rows of foxlike teeth."</b><br><br>I have had to deal with heroines, or called so, of all sorts. The fierce, the whiny, the hotheaded, the softie-and-swoony. The ones who can fight and the ones who cannot, the ones who can think and the ones who cannot; princesses, commoners, magicians, assassins, many, so many of them, and all different one from the other, for better or for worse.<br>But none, <i>none</i> of them even compare to<b> Kestrel</b>. The one with the cunning mind, all sharp thoughts and nimble ploys. The one who's dangerous not because of what she holds in her hand, but for what she hides up her sleeve. The one who, up until now, battled her heart for her heart's secret's sake, and who, finally, must no more.<br>Kestrel's done fighting herself. Now she fights <i>for</i> herself.<br>The one thing I didn't expect?<br>That Kestrel's mind, that <i>fierce creature of a mind</i>, would be her mightiest opponent. <br><br><b>"Your light happens to shine brighter. It's best for everyone if it goes out."</b><br><br>•Seeing Kestrel struggle with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her memory <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was strange, and totally<b> unexpected</b>. It added little to the <b>plot</b>, which, anyway, is not the focal point of the book -to the book's advantage, in my opinion: this trilogy is deliciously, very characteristically <b>character-driven</b>. This expedient, then, was so unexpected, so much as to give me pause at first, but then I saw the idea -fleeing, elusive, very Rutkoskian- lying beneath: it was the last round of Kestrel versus herself, but while before her enemy was her heart, now it's her mind she has to overcome. And we all know what an enemy that mind can be. <br><br><b>"She had no one to blame but herself."</b><br><br>Yes, it really was the last round. And her final victory was <b>glorious</b>. Because despite everything, despite the betrayal and the shattered heart, the childhood made of longing and one-sided adoration, the expectations unmet, the hollow hope, despite the <i>brokenness</i>, Kestrel wins.<br>And wins.<br>And wins.<br>I loved how she is finally able to get rid of her masks, give up her lies -see how perfectly the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[amnesia <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> device fits and serves the purpose- and, somehow, discover herself all over again. My heart was stolen by the sly, deceptive Kestrel of <i>The Winner's Curse</i> (which is still my favourite book in the trilogy). But this Kestrel? <b>True</b>. New and old at once. <b>Pure</b>. A red-hot blade upon raw flesh. <br>Rarely have I admired a character to the point of saying <i>I want to be like her</i>.<br>I want to be like her.<br><br>•<b>Arin</b>'s character undergoes a different, but somewhat parallel, kind of trials. The war, the gods, the blood on his hands: each of these things and many more are, to Arin, reasons to question himself, to briefly indulge his doubts and to swipe them away with a swing of his sword. <br><br><b>"He wanted to deafen the sounds. <i>Close your eyes</i>, he wanted to tell that child. The echo of old panic fluttered in Arin's chest."</b><br><br>He is <b>tormented</b>, but he never truly hesitates, never falters, and I didn't expect the awe that his ruthlessness inspired in me. Because Arin is gentle, full of tenderness and care, and yet, in some twisted way, violence suits him. He blames it on fate: what could a boy born in the year of death been born to, if not grief and blood? And Arin accepts it. Not only, but at first he may even be too prone to it. It's Kestrel to pull him back from the edge of the abyss, which served as a great means to the <b>development</b> of their <b>relationship</b>.<br>And while we are on the subject, favorite scene: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Arin melting his father's sword to forge a new dagger for Kestrel, to replace the one he'd cast into the sea. Don't quote me, but I cried <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>•I have diffusely exposed my reading of the main characters. What else do you want me to tell you about? Maybe how much I adore and how skilfully<b> fleshed-out </b>all the other <b>characters</b> are?<br><br>•The sparkling <b>bromance</b>?<br><br><b>"I’ve been thinking."<br>"Dear Gods."</b><br><br>•The flawless <b>balance</b> of the <b>pace</b>?<br><br>•Or maybe the <b>astounding writing</b>? The way Rutkoski's words unfold with the finest grace, fall upon your mind like the lightest feather or the sweetest beam of light? The way you're left staring, wordless because of words, at this little miracle made paper and ink? I could. I could try to explain what Rutkoski's writing can do to your soul, and I could do it with the wildest metaphors and most colorful analogies. The only thing that stops me is the awareness that it would be, alas, useless. It's <b>poetry</b>, and it's <b>painful</b>. That's all you have to know. The rest, you have to find out for yourself.<br>(I used to think I had my way with words -in my native language. Rutkoski, who, when it comes to words, is a deity, makes me feel ashamed of having ever thought such a fool thing.)<br><br>➽ I'll never shake this series off my heart, or off my mind, for that matter. I was so afraid when I started reading this book; it was because I was sure, <i>sure</i>, that Rutkoski would have made us suffer horribly. In a sense, she did, but she was merciful, and I am grateful. And I will reread the whole series soon. And I will keep thinking about it until that moment. <br>And after, too.<br>And after that too.<br><br><b>PRE-READ</b><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://fiercereads.com/books/the-winners-kiss/?utm_source=Instagram&amp;utm_medium=InstagramProfile&amp;utm_term=na&amp;utm_content=na_read_Excerpt-Online&amp;utm_campaign=9780374384739">http://fiercereads.com/books/the-winn...</a><br><br>This sneak peak, guys, THIS BLESSED SNEAK PEAK.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426164025ra/13982915.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah but I am scared to hope all the same. It's not like I trust Rutkoski with my little fragile heart.<br><br>Why does life have to be so freaking painful?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13530186045265032713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9840973343990847601">Rating has been raised to 2.5 stars.<br/><br/><b>*MAJOR SPOILERS AHEAD*</b><br/><br/>I think I finally understand how my parents feel about me. <br/><br/><b>D I S A P P O I N T E D</b> big fucking time man. <br/><br/>I feel like a totally different author wrote this book. Literally everything about this book seems so different and changed and you know what, I refuse to believe that this book is the ending to my most fucking favorite series (hint: The Winner's trilogy). <br/><br/>At the mines, Kestrel is given a drug with her meals and drinks that slowly make</span>
  <span id="freeText9840973343990847601" style="display:none">Rating has been raised to 2.5 stars.<br /><br /><b>*MAJOR SPOILERS AHEAD*</b><br /><br />I think I finally understand how my parents feel about me. <br /><br /><b>D I S A P P O I N T E D</b> big fucking time man. <br /><br />I feel like a totally different author wrote this book. Literally everything about this book seems so different and changed and you know what, I refuse to believe that this book is the ending to my most fucking favorite series (hint: The Winner's trilogy). <br /><br />At the mines, Kestrel is given a drug with her meals and drinks that slowly makes her lose her memories. (Like how even though?? Nothing's really explained about the drug.) The best thing about Kestrel was that she was clever, independent and she was very strong. She was strategic and smart when it came to politics and she was also quite stupid and flawed. She got caught, she failed, but she's not perfect and I loved that about her. But when she loses her memory, her character is just so not her. I understand that memory loss isn't her fault and I understand that she was not herself and I am okay with that, but this plot line takes half of the book up, and I was incredibly bored and disappointed.<br /><br />Honestly, the book could have done without the drugs and memory loss. First, there is no explanation about the drug and how it could be used for memory loss. (Shitty science) The memory loss plotline is super fucking long and takes up so much of the story and left me bored as fuck. It's like about the first half of the book and I was just bored out of my mind. <br /><br />I also really hated the romance. Arin and Kestrel felt so....forced together? I don't know, they just don't for together. I loved their romance when they were apart, but together they just didn't work out. (I think it was because Kestrel didn't remember him, maybe?) Anyways, everything was just very different and I didn't like it at all. <br /><br />Even the action scenes felt so boring. They weren't even filled with action.</span>
