<div id="review_1195749665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1195749665" />
    <a title="Cody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35007929-cody"><img alt="Cody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415626292p2/35007929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1195749665?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody" href="/user/show/35007929-cody">Cody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35007929-cody?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35007929-cody?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35007929-cody?shelf=to-be-released">to-be-released</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35007929-cody?shelf=ah-mazing">ah-mazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35007929-cody?shelf=love-love-love">love-love-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35007929-cody?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1195749665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15896153831865445231">The Winner’s Trilogy is without a doubt one of my favourite series ever, from its captivating writing, the incredible characters and those crafty plot twists, Rutkoski has proven with each new release that she can still leave us in a complete state of shock…. The same can definitely be said for The Winner’s Kiss; my dear friends, you may want to brace yourselves.<br/><br/> After the heart-breaking ending of The Winner’s Crime, Kestrel is in a barbaric work camp where she is drugged in order to work tirele</span>
  <span id="freeText15896153831865445231" style="display:none">The Winner’s Trilogy is without a doubt one of my favourite series ever, from its captivating writing, the incredible characters and those crafty plot twists, Rutkoski has proven with each new release that she can still leave us in a complete state of shock…. The same can definitely be said for The Winner’s Kiss; my dear friends, you may want to brace yourselves.<br /><br /> After the heart-breaking ending of The Winner’s Crime, Kestrel is in a barbaric work camp where she is drugged in order to work tirelessly long hours under the watch of ruthless guards. Arin knows nothing of Kestrel’s predicament; he’s too busy preparing his people for a War with Valoria. Arin will not lose his country without a fight and with his new alliance with Dacra and the god of Death on his side, he will be unstoppable.<br /><br />Kestrel will break your heart in this book; she has been a force to be reckoned with through this series, her clever wits and strategic mind have been her greatest weapons but I feel you don’t really know a character until you’ve witnessed them at their highs and lows--- let me tell you, Kestrel hits rock bottom but I am in awe of her strength and ability to get back up. Kestrel is truly a hero and a fantastic heroine.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“She'd betrayed her country because she'd believed it was the right thing to do. Yet would she have done this, if not for Arin?<br />He knew none of it. Had never asked for it. Kestrel had made her own choices. <br />It was unfair to blame him.<br />But she wanted to.”</i>
</b><br /><br /> Arin’s greatest enemy is himself, he continues to doubt himself and any decision he makes, after his last meeting with Kestrel he’s always looking for a hidden meaning in people’s action and words. Arin struggles trying to lead a war where he is outgunned and outnumbered but he is able to be just a devious as Kestrel and I loved seeing his brilliant mind at work.<br /><br />The romance, oh you guys!!!! <b>The Winner’s KISS is a befitting title.</b> Kestrel and Arin are one of my top ships and I have wanted to smush them together since the beginning. Their romance is so slow and it’s been full of disaster and complications but they are perfect together and they are so deserving of each other. Fellow shippers and fangirls will be very, very, very happy, <i>eeeeekkk!</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“He changed us both." She seemed to struggle for words. "I think of you, all that you lost, who you were, what you were forced to be, and might have been, and I—I have become this, this person, unable to—<br />She shut her mouth."<br /><br />"Kestrel," he said softly, "I love this person.”</i>
</b><br /><br /> The action never stops, from the very beginning you can feel the high stakes of this dangerous game Arin and Kestrel play but my OTP plays to win so be prepared for some epic and sometimes intense scenes that will have you holding your breath.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Did you have to bring the tiger?”<br /><br />“I kept him hungry during the journey here, just for you,” Roshar said. “Go give him a nice snuggle, won’t you? He’s come all this way to see you. The least you could do is give him one of your arms to eat. Too much? What about a hand? At least some fingers. Arin, where’s your hospitality?”<br /><br />Arin, laughing, embraced his friend.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I’ve got to say that I have a new favourite pairing within this series: <b>Arin and Roshar</b>. Oh my god, the relationship between these two it’s utterly hilarious and fantastic, I found myself excited for their next interaction. It’s filled with friendly banter, backhanded compliments and lots and lots of sass and sarcasm. Roshar became a main character in this book; he has in own struggles within his kingdom and family, trying to figure out where his own alliances lie but the friendship with him and Arin was extremely heartwarming, I felt so spoiled for all his page time. <b>Can we please have book for Roshar? Please Rutkoksi, I am begging you!</b><br /><br /> The Winner’s Kiss is the best book of the series and best way to end a trilogy, it was completely perfect, and faultless! <s>Well, Roshar’s story would be nice.</s> I can’t even put into words how sad I am to see this beautiful series come to an end, <b>I am in no way ready</b> to say goodbye to Arin and Kestrel and <b>I’m also in no way ready</b> to be parted with Rutkoski’s magical writing, I am praying to all of Arin’s Gods for her to have some crafty series up her sleeves. The Winner’s Kiss will make you cry, laugh, cry some more, warm your heart and cry some more, it’s an extraordinary ending and I am so thankful to have read this early but for also picking this up in the first place. It’s been one hell of a ride but I couldn’t have asked for more, now go read it and enjoy!!<br /><br /><a href="http://literary-lyobsessed.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary-ly Obsessed (Blog)</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/CodyLeighDuffy" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/codyleighduffy/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15896153831865445231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_921031654" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/921031654" />
    <a title="Sophie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie"><img alt="Sophie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564510350p2/8563233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/921031654?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie">Sophie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408858745" href="/book/show/25526307-the-winner-s-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer921031654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10014736202622896847">I received an Advance Reader Copy via NetGalley. This in no way impacted on my view.<br/><br/>I'm sure it will be no surprise that I loved this book. I don't think I know anyone who hasn't loved this series, and when I found out that The Winner's Kiss was up on NetGalley, I requested it so quickly. I was in the library doing research for an assignment when I got the email came through that I'd been approved, and let me tell you, it was extremely difficult to keep my attention on civil war battles when I k</span>
  <span id="freeText10014736202622896847" style="display:none">I received an Advance Reader Copy via NetGalley. This in no way impacted on my view.<br /><br />I'm sure it will be no surprise that I loved this book. I don't think I know anyone who hasn't loved this series, and when I found out that The Winner's Kiss was up on NetGalley, I requested it so quickly. I was in the library doing research for an assignment when I got the email came through that I'd been approved, and let me tell you, it was extremely difficult to keep my attention on civil war battles when I knew I could read about Kestrel and Arin.<br /><br />I've put off reviewing this book for a few weeks because I just can't organise my thoughts. Basically, the book was amazing, I loved it, and I'm sad the series is over.<br /><br />In The Winner's Kiss, we dive back in just after the dramatic events of The Winner's Crime. Kestrel is on her way to the work camps in the north for her treason against the Valorians, and Arin has no idea as he's heading to defend Herrani. The final battle between Valoria and Herran is coming, and both with be crucial players in it. There's a lot of angst, and some quite sweet moments, but basically, I was a complete mess while reading it.<br /><br />Kestrel remains one of my favourite YA heroines ever! As you can imagine, she had a quite tough time in this book, especially at the beginning, but she remained strong, even in her vulnerability. There were moments when my heart just broke whilst reading her PoV chapters, and I loved seeing her grow, and come to terms with the fact that her native Valorian people aren't the best, and she has more connection with the Herrani in reality.<br /><br />Arin, well, he had to deal with a lot in this book too. He's the leader of the Herrani people, and has to come to terms with his responsibility to his people. At the same time, he's struggling with his feelings for Kestrel, especially when he thinks she is the cause of all his problems. When they finally come together again, both struggle with wanting to help the Herrani cause, when they can't really deal with their own issues.<br /><br />The Winner's Kiss had a plot line that was simply sublime. So much was happening, but not too much that you couldn't keep up. After the action packed books 1 &amp; 2, I didn't know how Marie could up the ante, but she definitely succeeded. Everything happened like I wished, and I can honestly say that I couldn't ask for more. The fact that Marie has done so much research whilst writing this book, including reading some of my favourite classical books, like Herodotus' The Histories, made it all the more better. The Winner's Trilogy will remain one of my all time favourite fantasy YA series, and I will basically shove it down everyone's throats until you pick up this series, and discover just how amazing it is. If I could, I would give it much more that 5 stars, it deserves all the stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10014736202622896847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1540921108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1540921108" />
    <a title="☆☽Erica☾☆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41218534-erica"><img alt="☆☽Erica☾☆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469208889p2/41218534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1540921108?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☆☽Erica☾☆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☆☽Erica☾☆" href="/user/show/41218534-erica">☆☽Erica☾☆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41218534-erica?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41218534-erica?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41218534-erica?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540921108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15607067374005237822"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459346725ra/18600302.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>I am writing this as a ghost because this book killed me.</b> <br/>I, Erica's ghost, have a lot of things to say about this but feel inadequate to verbalize my love/obsession/adoration/fascination with this spectacular story using coherent thought. Some other reviews somehow managed this, such as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080615802' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nina's</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1361831551?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Simona's</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556713428' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chantal's</a>. <br/><br/><i>But I shall try.</i><br/><br/>To begin, I would like to say that I read this for about 7 hours straight. I ignored the existence of time to fulfill my addiction to this series, which is, hones</span>
  <span id="freeText15607067374005237822" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459346725ra/18600302.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I am writing this as a ghost because this book killed me.</b> <br>I, Erica's ghost, have a lot of things to say about this but feel inadequate to verbalize my love/obsession/adoration/fascination with this spectacular story using coherent thought. Some other reviews somehow managed this, such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080615802" rel="nofollow noopener">Nina's</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1361831551?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Simona's</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556713428" rel="nofollow noopener">Chantal's</a>. <br><br><i>But I shall try.</i><br><br>To begin, I would like to say that I read this for about 7 hours straight. I ignored the existence of time to fulfill my addiction to this series, which is, honestly, <i>my favorite series I've ever read.</i> I cannot understand how I lived without this series and, for so long, without being a devoted reader of anything. <b>This series embodies what truly is magical about reading. It embodies the true transformative power of a story. And embodies how a reader can fall deeply in love with fictional characters.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403442774ra/10094013.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You may be saying to yourself, ghost of Erica, you're being awfully dramatic here, it can't possibly be that good. And I would say to that: <i>First of all,</i><br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459348289ra/18600543.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Second of all</i>, <b>no</b> I'm <i>not</i> over-hyping this.<br><br>The Winner's Kiss was a <b>perfect</b> ending to a <b>perfect</b> series. This final installment continued with the political intrigue and overall complexity that the first two had built so well. If the author bombed after the first book, the original story would have still been great. But noooooo, she didn't stop there. She made the story <b>absolutely fucking spectacular.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451566950ra/17559254.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh so often authors stretch out their series by adding unnecessary drama (i.e. personal relationships or magical worlds getting in the way) but Marie Rutkoski made a story where the conflicts were, however extraordinary, ultimately understandable. I did not facepalm at events. I did not roll my eyes at people's choices. I was, at times, crushed by certain occurrences, but they were necessary events in the end.<br><br><b>The true star here was our female protagonist, Kestrel.</b> She was spectacular. And no, she wasn't a magical assassin or the chosen one or the lost princess who possesses a legendary power, she was a dynamic, vibrant, brave, manipulative, powerful person with flaws and misjudgments and worries. And we hardly are ever <i>told</i> these traits, we are able to see them ourselves. <b>Kestrel is shown to us as a complex individual whose attributes come through in her actions and thoughts, not through direct communication from the author.</b><br><blockquote>
<b><i>“You don't need to be gifted with a blade. You are your own best weapon.”</i></b> </blockquote><br>She is a beautifully crafted character. Her development over the series made me feel embarrassed that my original love for her in <i>The Winner's Curse</i> was so shallow. I didn't know her then. I didn't see all she could do. But I am thankful I got to see her evolution. And she's probably off doing more badass things now even though the series ended. <br><br>Ultimately, I think that this whole series has the overarching theme of the transformative power of love. And no, not like in typical YA novels where hot 17-year-old girl becomes transfixed with shirtless hot 17-year-old boy and they get married at the end. I mean love in all forms. The love between a father and daughter, between friends, humorous bromance, dependable allies, love that hurts but love that heals, and, lastly, romantic love. I know people often say shit like "love hurts" or "love is a battlefield" or "love is pain." And I guess I could see what they mean, relationships are difficult, they take work. Sometimes really passionate (yet unhealthy) relationships cause you immense turmoil. I've experienced it. BUT ultimately those people are being dumb. Love inherently does not hurt. When it is twisted in such a way, something you view as love feels bad when it is unrequited. Love is beautiful and feels good and lights your soul. Yes, it has trials, yes things hurt sometimes, but love is a force of good. It makes you a better person on your own, to be supported by a person who unconditionally loves you. This book knows that. It is full of prime examples of this love at work, in its many forms. And the love between Kestrel and Arin is that kind of love, the true kind. They grow together and feel together and move forward with each other's best interests at heart.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392122081ra/8503822.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But the fucking suspense sometimes. Like I was pretty much internally begging the author to bring Kestrel and Arin together.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459346725i/18600304.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And none of this emotion would have been possible without the brilliant writing. <b>Marie Rutkoski is one hell of a writer. Her writing motivates me to be a better writer AND a better reader.</b> She masterfully constructed this story. She took a story that could eventually fall flat and made it pulse with life. Her words were poetic and beautiful and symbolic and powerful without being overwhelming. And she utilized POV changes with expertise. I especially loved when in battle she shifted from Kestrel's point of view to Arin's at the most poignant times. It hastened the plot and created that sense of urgency one (I'm guessing) would feel in battle. It conveyed the illusion that many, many things were happening at once and her narrative camera was keeping you on the edge of your seat. Even within simple conversations, her suggestion of pauses and reactions was brilliant. She <i>makes</i> the reader intelligent, because she forces you to think and become enraptured in this world. For example look at this:<br><blockquote>
  <i>“How do I look in the dark?”<br><br>Startled, Arin glanced at him. The question had had no edges. It wasn’t sleek, either. Its soft, uncertain shape suggested that Roshar truly wanted to know. In the fired red shadows, his limbs looked lax and his mutilated face met Arin’s squarely. The heavy feeling that Arin carried—that specific sadness, nestled just below his collar bone, like a pendant—lessened. He said, “Like my friend.”<br><br>Roshar didn’t smile. When he spoke, his voice matched his expression, which was rare for him. Rarer still: his tone. Quiet and true. “You do, too.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Like what. How does she verbalize brilliance in this way? I'm astounded. Bottom line, she's an incredible writer and I'm honored that she signed my first two books in the series (and that she's friends with Kristin Cashore whom I love). There's a particular quote that I absolutely adore that I wanted to share with you all (the bolding in this passage is my own): <blockquote>
<i>The stained-glass window glowed, and something eased open inside Kestrel. As color seeped into the room, she felt an unexpected wish.<br>She wished her father were here.</i><br>You, who seek your own father's death.<br><i>But she didn't, she found that she couldn't, no matter how he had hurt her. She wished that he could see her play, and win. That he could see what she saw now.<br><b>A window is just a window. Colored glass: mere glass. But in the sun it becomes more. She would show him, and say, love should do</b></i> this.<br><i>And you too, she would tell him, because she could no longer deny that it remained true, in spite of everything.<br>I love you, too.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>This passage made me falter when I read it. It is so <b>
  <i>beautiful</i>
</b>. And so indicative of the overarching theme of genuine love that weaves itself throughout every aspect of this story. Viewing love as the effect sunlight has on a stained glass window is something not only visually appealing, but also breathtakingly true and pure. As I said before, love should make you glow with light.<br><br>I could keep going. But I think you get the picture. You should prob hop on this magical, literary train.<br><br><b>It was an absolutely divine pleasure to read this series. Thank you, Marie Rutkoski.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458928786ra/18551180.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>******<b>4/9/16 addition</b>*******<br><br>Sooo look I met Marie Rutkoski!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460251212i/18718630._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15607067374005237822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1719433179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1719433179" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1719433179?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408858745" href="/book/show/25526307-the-winner-s-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-and-a-half-stars">1-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1719433179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17738404923773175144">Well, cancel 2017.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/02/04/the-winners-kiss-review/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>What do you rate a book when you’re saddened to your core that you finished the series, but also you didn’t enjoy it and thought it was objectively not good? WHAT DO I DO? It’s like mourning a childhood friend who turned out to be a meninist, or a My Little Pony fan, or a fan of buttered popcorn-flavored jelly beans. You know, something definitively but somewhat harmlessly Bad™.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483314081ra/21600399.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>God, I love that gif. Okay. Okay okay okay. I’m going to try </span>
  <span id="freeText17738404923773175144" style="display:none">Well, cancel 2017.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/02/04/the-winners-kiss-review/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br><br>What do you rate a book when you’re saddened to your core that you finished the series, but also you didn’t enjoy it and thought it was objectively not good? WHAT DO I DO? It’s like mourning a childhood friend who turned out to be a meninist, or a My Little Pony fan, or a fan of buttered popcorn-flavored jelly beans. You know, something definitively but somewhat harmlessly Bad™.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483314081ra/21600399.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>God, I love that gif. Okay. Okay okay okay. I’m going to try to coalesce approximately 1,472,389 emotions into a review here. Oh this is so hard. Oh I don’t want to write this. This review might be really bad, you guys. (Also I was in denial for roughly 60% of the book about the fact that I wasn’t liking it and thereby refused to take notes. So. Really making it hard on myself.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484511097ra/21725401.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m just going to jump into it. My BIGGEST ISSUE - the type of problem that makes you scoff and turn your nose up even when you’re alone - was stupid Arin. (Yes, the one who narrates 50% of this book.) I’m furious about this. I never <i>loved</i> Arin, though. He’s always been a touch too angsty and obsessive. But, you know, whatever. The surprising thing is that despite this guy creeping me out, I still lowkey shipped him and Kestrel. This book forced me to realize that I only <s>tattooed Arin + Kestrel 5ever on my lower back</s> supported them when they were apart. Because they don’t work well together, like, at all.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484511097ra/21725402.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Exactly, LC! Thank you. Congratulations on your pregnancy.) Anyway, why are they not good together, you ask? Well, it’s Arin’s dumb fault. A good relationship - okay, wait. I want to clarify here that I’m making a sweeping generalization about love in YA fantasy, NOT giving unsubstantiated relationship advice. Despite my charm, charisma, beauty, and immense skill at review-writing, I’m not qualified for that shit. OKAY, so a good relationship in books consists of the two characters supporting each other. Having each other’s backs. Synonyms. But Arin is never supportive of Kestrel. This book takes place during a WAR, and every time Kestrel tries to do ANYTHING - like, make a plan, sneak around, or GOD FORBID go to battle - he spends 20 pages moping and begging her not to go. UGH. SHE’S A BADASS. SHUT THE F*CK UP FOR ONCE ARIN.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484511097ra/21725403.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So...Kestrel. Her badassery got her into the exclusive club of my all-time-favorite-female characters list in the second book. The central aspect of her character is that she is not physically a badass, but her political and intelligent mind TOTALLY is. That’s an amazing foundation for a character. That’s my dream version of myself. But...she felt reduced in this book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383095354ra/6387152.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kestrel starts off this book in a work camp - one thing this book did well is the work camp trope, which didn’t get too repetitive or last too long - and becomes addicted to the drugs she is force fed. This addiction causes her to lose her memory. (Shoddy science but GOD you have to accept it in YA fantasy, no?) The memory loss plotline takes <i>forever</i> and is so boring. It also reduces the best part of her character, which, sorry, is just a bad writing choice. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And so disappears my favorite part of the last one.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484511097ra/21725404.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don’t talk about writing style a lot in reviews, and when I do, it’s usually a positive. It’s not my intention to cast blame on YA books - I goddamn love them, bro - but a lot of the YA I’ve been reading of late has been stylistically unremarkable. I think that’s an asset to young adult books, as it helps with pacing, clarity and level of difficulty. But this book was written <i>bonkers</i>-ly. (Yes, I just attempted to use bonkers as an adverb. What of it?!)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392755670ra/8605747.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>First off, this book was TEEMING with the world’s longest sentences. I’m talking paragraphs of just a single run-on, baby! I wasn’t even mad so much as fascinated - like, this sentence is six lines long without so much as a comma? Bananas!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427716156ra/14311010.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What really bugged me was how <i>overwrought</i> it was. This isn’t the kind of overwrought I talked about in my review of I’ll Meet You There, where every single moment is emotionally significant...although there was a lot of that, too. I’m talking about the sheer amount of figurative language put to work in this book. I have never read so many similes in my life. Marie Rutkoski, don’t think I didn’t notice you say make three separate comparisons between something and an egg. And these aren’t just the usual, dumb YA similes, like “his eyes were like chocolate” or “her hair shone like gold.” Here’s an example of one I literally just found on the random page I flipped to: “A feeling floated over him like sillage from a rare perfume. He seemed to hear the tinkle of a glass stopper lifted from a tiny flacon. The release of scent. How was it possible, to smell flowers that weren’t there?”<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484511097ra/21725405.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Everything is profound, everything is a simile, everything is a runon. For almost 500 pages. It was EXHAUSTING. I never wanted to be angry at this book, and so getting angry at it made me even angrier. And on and on, even more egg comparisons and sweeping, tryhard generalizations about ~life~. Flipped to another random page, and: Kestrel “wondered if there was any difference between how she listened to [her father] and how Arin listened to his god.” Um, yes, many differences. Just because it sounds smart doesn’t mean it’s deep. Or accurate. Or NOT DUMB.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484511097ra/21725406.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But this book does have one impressive thing about it: it manages to be pure, unadulterated boring while a WAR IS GOING ON. Even the battle scenes are just eh, nowhere near enough to make up for the countless pages of Kestrel and Arin making goo-goo eyes at each other. There was just so much romance in this book. I’m getting physically sick just thinking about it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448374647ra/17131583.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This just...got rid of everything I liked about the last one. The intrigue, the action, Kestrel’s cunning, the politics, the lack of romance, me not wanting to straight up murder Arin. I’m so, so, SO upset and I’m canceling this year. Four disappointments in a row.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484511097ra/21725407.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bottom line: I’m not giving this book one star only because I liked the last one SO MUCH. And I still think people should read this series. Maybe you’ll even like this book! But to make this all about me, as I so love to do: I really needed to love this book and I SUPER didn't.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17738404923773175144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1080615802" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080615802" />
    <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway"><img alt="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456070558p2/32524334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1080615802?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway">Nina (Every Word A Doorway)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408858745" href="/book/show/25526307-the-winner-s-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=2016-faves">2016-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=my-armada-of-ships">my-armada-of-ships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1080615802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7999430875351066014"><b>Fellow readers and fangirls, I have come to preach to you the awesomeness that is this book, this series, this writer. And I’ve come armed. With words. And feels. And quotes.</b><br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/feels' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449270699ra/17258575.gif' alt='feels photo: tumblr_inline_mfkq86L8zl1qg61c1_zps68a607fc.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>The Winner’s Curse</i> was a gentle introduction to the characters, the world and the romance. I loved it. <i>The Winner’s Crime</i> was a crescendo of court intrigue, sticky webs of lies and the first glimpses of war. I loved it. <i>The Winner’s Kiss</i> was a battle cry. I loved it. <br/><br/>I had <b>astronomical expectations</b> for this book, and it </span>
  <span id="freeText7999430875351066014" style="display:none"><b>Fellow readers and fangirls, I have come to preach to you the awesomeness that is this book, this series, this writer. And I’ve come armed. With words. And feels. And quotes.</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/feels" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449270699ra/17258575.gif" alt="feels photo: tumblr_inline_mfkq86L8zl1qg61c1_zps68a607fc.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>The Winner’s Curse</i> was a gentle introduction to the characters, the world and the romance. I loved it. <i>The Winner’s Crime</i> was a crescendo of court intrigue, sticky webs of lies and the first glimpses of war. I loved it. <i>The Winner’s Kiss</i> was a battle cry. I loved it. <br><br>I had <b>astronomical expectations</b> for this book, and it did not disappoint. <b>Frankly, I would rate this 6 stars if I could.</b> My words will never do this beautiful gem of a book justice, just to give you a fair warning before you plunge into my review (Also: if you want to be kept completely in the dark, then don't read this until you've read the book). <br><br><br><b>
  <u>Kestrel</u>
</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>Once there was a girl who was too sure of herself. Not everyone would call her beautiful, but they admitted that she had a certain grace that intimidated more often than it charmed. She was not, society agreed, someone you wanted to cross.</i>
</blockquote> <b>This version of Kestrel was probably the one I liked the most.</b> She has always been a fierce, cunning character but in <i>The Winner’s Curse</i>, she was rather tame, and in the <i>The Winner’s Crime</i>, she was deceitful. In this book, she was neither. Rutkoski adds a nice little twist to her personal subplot, which allows Kestrel to uncoil like a tight knot. Her journey is hard and painful, and I suffered alongside one of my favourite female characters of all time like I haven’t in a long time (the book lid has finger imprints on both sides from gripping it so hard). Her broken relationships – with Arin, with her father – are thoroughly explored through her eyes. <b>What I still love most about Kestrel is that she is a strong opponent in spite of her physical incapability with a weapon.</b> Do you know why I think she no longer holds a sword on this cover? Because she doesn’t need the bloody thing. <br><blockquote>
  <i> “You don't need to be gifted with a blade. You are your own best weapon.” </i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Arin</u>
</b><br><br>After the <i>The Winner’s Crime</i>, I didn’t hold much love for Arin. He’d been blinded by jealousy, and it had disappointed me because Arin can be a cunning badass if he wants to. In <i>The Winner’s Kiss</i>, he’s finally thinking straight again. <b>This book is as much about self-discovery for Kestrel as it is for Arin.</b> For the most part of the series, Arin has been a gentle character despite his iron determination. <b>Now that war is upon him, Arin discovers a ferocious side of him</b> – one that revels in the rush of battle, one that kills without mercy. This characteristic emerges without suppressing his other qualities: His protectiveness, his loyalty, his morals. To witness Arin’s development throughout the book was both beautiful and heartbreaking. <br><blockquote>
<i>Arin’s god slapped him across the face.<br></i>Pay attention,<i> death demanded.<br>Arin did, and after that, no one could touch him.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Roshar</u>
</b><br><br>Introduced in <i>The Winner’s Crime</i> (in a not especially memorable way), Roshar was a necessity to this instalment like we need air to breathe. <b>His witty, snarky character provides an excellent balance to Arin’s calm nature.</b> Roshar has an air of combined arrogance and modesty. <b>He rides to war armed with his sword and his sass</b> – now can anyone tell me whether there is anything more satisfying than that? No? No. (He reminded me a bit of Sturmhond, to be honest.) <br><blockquote>
  <i> “I happen to be very good at war. It’s because I’m so handsome. Like one of your gods. People see me and their minds go blank. I run my sword right through them.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>The friendships</u>
</b><br><br>The predominant friendship in this book is Arin’s and Roshar’s, two buddies at war, commanders of an army, destroyers of Valorians. The banter between the two of them reminded me of Kell and Rhy. They have this <b>bromantic chemistry</b>, making it hard for those facial muscles to stay relaxed. <br><blockquote>
  <i>Roshar lay on his back, the dip of his neck bolstered by a tied bedroll. He smoked. “I’ve been thinking.”<br>“Dear Gods.”<br>“It occurs to me that you have no official rank, and that I, as you prince, might give you one.” He said an eastern word Arin didn’t know. “Well? Will it suit?”<br>“Depends.”<br>“On?”<br>“Whether that word was some horrific insult you’re pretending is an actual military rank.” </i>
</blockquote> A more surprising friendship arose between Kestrel and Sarsine, two equally fierce women. The female friendship snuck up on the characters on its tiptoes, slow and tentative. <b>The affection they hold for each other is heart-warming.</b><br><blockquote>Protective. <i>That was the word for Sarsine’s furrowed brow, her gentle mouth. <br>“Does something else trouble you?” she asked. “You can talk to me. I can keep a secret.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>The romance</u>
</b><br><br>The sequel had left Kestrel and Arin torn, torn as individuals, torn from each other. I had a lot of Jack-Sparrow moments where I kept bellowing, “Stop blowing holes in my ship!” I was not sure they would ever get passed this but, as I said, <b>Marie Rutkoski weaves in little twists that somehow slowly build a bridge over the gaping hole dug by distrust and resentment.</b> I fiercely adore these two beautiful people together. <br><blockquote>
  <i> “Do I still own you?”<br>“Yes.”</i>
</blockquote> Rutkoski made it clear that it was not the war that was keeping them apart – it was them. In <i>The Winner’s Curse</i>, they had been on different sides. In <i>The Winner’s Crime</i>, their communication had been completely severed. In <i>The Winner’s Kiss</i>, there was a lot of growth, forgiveness and mutual respect. <b>Their relationship development devoted a lot of time to the acknowledgement of the other person’s faults, strengths and beliefs.</b> I especially liked how the clash of Arin’s belief in his Gods with Kestrel’s apparent disbelief was handled. <b>They did not just grow as individuals, they rose above as one.</b> <br><blockquote>
  <i>“I trust you. You won’t lie to me.”</i>
</blockquote> And the last scene of the book is so incredibly beautiful. My heart swelled to twice its size. I think I need to go see a cardiologist to check whether my heart is still working properly.<br><br><b>
  <u>The storyline</u>
</b><br><br>The plot was engaging. <b>The atmosphere of war and hardship is palpable.</b> Rutkoski constructs a powerful storyline of politics, strategies and battles, underpinned by her beautiful, metaphoric writing. <b>The friendships and romance never overpower the plot and vice versa.</b> There was enough room for everything. The pace was steady and never stuttered. <b>The world-building fully unfurled in this instalment. The plot twists were the death of me.</b> The tension building towards the climax gripped me like an iron fist and would not let go until almost the very end. <br> <br><br><b>This is one of the most HEARTBREAKING and GUT-WRENCHING, UNIQUE and BEAUTIFUL series I’ve ever read. Rutkoski’s skill for the written word and the flawed, relatable characters she crafted are out of this world. The finale was the fireworks this wondrous journey deserved. Utter perfection. I will push this series on any- and everyone.</b><br><br>(Has anyone paid attention to how many times I dropped the word “beautiful”? In case you’re interested: It was 7 times).<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><b>
  <u>Preview</u>
</b><br>Dear Ms Rutkoski, <br>as you are no stranger to cruelty yourself (yes, I am referring to the ending of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443207.The_Winner_s_Crime__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___2_" title="The Winner's Crime (The Winner's Trilogy, #2) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Crime</a>), you may understand that if I don't get <i>"Arin+Kestrel, unharmed, reunited"</i>, I <b>will</b> do very unkind things to your book. Or I might hack your computer and rewrite the ending – oh, and possibly change that corny crap you chose for a title while I'm at it. (Although the latter might technically be the publisher's fault but shhh). <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/jennifer%20lawrence" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418661662ra/12865777.gif" alt="jennifer lawrence photo: Crazy tumblr_inline_minh0m5hCU1qz4rgp_zps3c935274.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>You've been warned. <b>Do not cross me.</b><br><br>That cover. <s>Weakness. Defeat. Surrender.</s> KESTREL, NOW WOULD BE THE TIME TO PICK UP THAT SWORD AND SLAY. And that bluuurb. <i>"… and a fragile hope."</i> – I can't even. Just can't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7999430875351066014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1794503857896770768">After that ending of The Winner's Crime, I was dying to get my greedy hands on this book and I could never have expected what we got.<br/><br/>The feels start right from the beginning and it's a rollercoaster that lasts the entire book. I have loved Kestrel and Arin and I loved seeing how much they've grown from book 1. They're different, yet the same. And can I please get a novella or spin off with all of the Roshar? I floved every single scene with him.<br/><br/>Please excuse my vague review, I would never want t</span>
  <span id="freeText1794503857896770768" style="display:none">After that ending of The Winner's Crime, I was dying to get my greedy hands on this book and I could never have expected what we got.<br /><br />The feels start right from the beginning and it's a rollercoaster that lasts the entire book. I have loved Kestrel and Arin and I loved seeing how much they've grown from book 1. They're different, yet the same. And can I please get a novella or spin off with all of the Roshar? I floved every single scene with him.<br /><br />Please excuse my vague review, I would never want to spoil this for anyone. Marie has created an amazing world and she's given us quite a ride. This book is a perfect example of how you end a trilogy.<br /><br />**Huge thanks to Macmillan for the invite to read**</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1371495264?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen" href="/user/show/10762033-maureen">Maureen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1371495264" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14281875049399399670">This may even be 4.5/5 stars but it just wasn't quite there for me though it was prETTY STINKING CLOSE.<br/><br/>I am a ball of emotions guys. I cried MULTIPLE times in this book from lots of feELINGS. <br/><br/>Kestrel is seriously one of my favorite protagonists ever. She's smart strategically and doesn't let anyone tell her what she can and cannot do - and she's not *totally* adept at fighting, though she is competent, but her real strength lies in her amazing ability to play the political game.<br/><br/>I also love Arin,</span>
  <span id="freeText14281875049399399670" style="display:none">This may even be 4.5/5 stars but it just wasn't quite there for me though it was prETTY STINKING CLOSE.<br /><br />I am a ball of emotions guys. I cried MULTIPLE times in this book from lots of feELINGS. <br /><br />Kestrel is seriously one of my favorite protagonists ever. She's smart strategically and doesn't let anyone tell her what she can and cannot do - and she's not *totally* adept at fighting, though she is competent, but her real strength lies in her amazing ability to play the political game.<br /><br />I also love Arin, how can you NOT? And I feel like a lot of the side characters (Sarsine, Roshar, etc) got a lot more fleshed out in this book and I really loved getting to know them.<br /><br />The plot was great, though the pacing was a little off for me. It didn't jump well from REALLY INTENSE to just chill time, it felt a little jagged between the two, but overall I liked the plot! Though I do love me some ARIN and KESTREL, the book bored me at times (OMG WHAT) but the other amazing parts almost made up for it.<br /><br />Overall really happy with this close to the series, but I don't know if any of the books will capture me and have the same magic for me as the first book. But still SOLID SOLID series that I would highly recommend.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10230039358842443458"><blockquote>
  <i>“Arin pulled her onto his lap. He held her shaking form, tucked his face into the crook of her cold neck as she sobbed against him. He murmured that he loved her more than he could say. He promised that he would always choose her first.” </i>
</blockquote><br/><b>5 Shining Stars!</b><br/><br/>The Winner's Kiss is the <b>best</b> and the <b>most emotional</b> book in the series, so prepare your tissues before starting to read it! I was an emotional mess after The Winner's Crime and I'd thought that The Winner's Kiss can't make my situation any w</span>
  <span id="freeText10230039358842443458" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Arin pulled her onto his lap. He held her shaking form, tucked his face into the crook of her cold neck as she sobbed against him. He murmured that he loved her more than he could say. He promised that he would always choose her first.” </i>
</blockquote><br><b>5 Shining Stars!</b><br><br>The Winner's Kiss is the <b>best</b> and the <b>most emotional</b> book in the series, so prepare your tissues before starting to read it! I was an emotional mess after The Winner's Crime and I'd thought that The Winner's Kiss can't make my situation any worse,however I was wrong (as usual).<br>Let me tell you what this book did to my heart;<br>It took my heart gently from my chest,patted it, then threw it to a wall, then said sorry and put a band aid on it, after that it shattered it, burned it down to ashes and finally dabbled it to sea. This is the summary of it!<br><br>After reading this book too, I can finally say that Kestrel is in my list of top 3 favourite protagonists. She was everything that I've wanted in this book and series. Her intelligence will always impress and influence me. She was so far one of the strongest characters I've ever read of.<br>Arin was as good as Kestrel. I loved his character even more after finishing the book. Both Kestrel and Arin are so lucky to have eachother after what they've been through.<br><br>Roshar is friend goals. I loved his character, his humor and his friendship with Arin. I loved how he used sarcasm even in the worst of times and how he cared for the people who he love and did no matter what for them. <br><blockquote>
  <i><br>“You could offer her a seat,” Arin said.<br>“Ah, but I have only two chairs in my tent, little Herrani, and we are three. I suppose she could always sit on your lap.” <br></i>
</blockquote><br>Oh and he and tiger Arin are definitely relationship goals.<br><br>Verex was another precious cinnamon roll. I am very glad that how we saw more of him in this book. He finally had the happy ending he deserved.<br><br>As for Kestrel's father, I don't know what to say nor think. I still don't understand his motives in The Winner's Crime and The Winner's Kiss, I honestly have no idea how I'd react if what happened to Kestrel happened to me. <br><blockquote>
  <i>“She would never give him her dagger. “I tried so hard to live in your world,” she told him. “Now it’s your turn to live in mine.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I hope he and Kestrel will find their peace in their situation as the time goes on.<br><br>I don't know what I'll do with my life anymore, I am so attached to this characters and to this world :( <br>I feel so sad and feel like I'll cry even if I got the ending that I wanted. I just don't want this to be over...<br>Thank you Marie Rutkoski for giving me the opportunity to read about awsome characters like Kestrel and Arin, I'll never forget their journey.<br>If you haven't read this book or this series still... what exactly are you doing with your life? stop whatever you're doing and read this ASAP! <br>And now I have this one question in my mind... what will I read now? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491914020ra/22460932.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462551590ra/19013197.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1589103613" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1589103613" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1589103613?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=best-young-adult">best-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=trilogy">trilogy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=messed-me-up">messed-me-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=multi-pov">multi-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=upper-ya">upper-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1589103613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10341579848589029377"><p>Buddy read with my partners in suffering <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1589110729' rel='nofollow noopener'>Katerina</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469445263' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vera</a>. Thank you, girls, for helping me survive this book *hearty hug*<br/></p><p><b>Actual rating: 5+</b><br/><b><i><blockquote>You don’t need to be gifted with a blade. You are your own best weapon.”</blockquote></i></b><br/> If you know me, you probably know that my two most favorite book series are ending this year. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_' title='The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven Boys</a> and The winner's trilogy. It's hard because they end a mere month from each other. An emotional blow. <i>The Winner's kiss's</i> time is up. It's <b>the hardest review I have ever written</b>, n</p></span>
  <span id="freeText10341579848589029377" style="display:none"><p>Buddy read with my partners in suffering <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1589110729" rel="nofollow noopener">Katerina</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469445263" rel="nofollow noopener">Vera</a>. Thank you, girls, for helping me survive this book *hearty hug*<br /></p><p><b>Actual rating: 5+</b><br /><b><i><blockquote>You don’t need to be gifted with a blade. You are your own best weapon.”</blockquote></i></b><br /> If you know me, you probably know that my two most favorite book series are ending this year. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> and The winner's trilogy. It's hard because they end a mere month from each other. An emotional blow. <i>The Winner's kiss's</i> time is up. It's <b>the hardest review I have ever written</b>, not because I don't have thoughts about the book, no, because it <b>physically hurts</b> to write my thoughts down, to accept that this is the end, nothing else is here for me. <i><b>I warn you, this review is going to be an emotional wreck. </b></i><br /></p><p>When I first read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/867473559" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a> I was instantly enchanted by the story, from the first words it was "my thing". It penetrated my heart, ripped it out and held it hostage for almost three years. I, like a girl from a fairy tale, put my heart inside an ivory box and gave it to this series. <i>The Winner's kiss</i> now returns my heart to me - torn and shredded - but I don't want it back, not yet. <b>You may ask, what is it about these books that makes me so possessed?</b> I can answer: <b>its characters</b>, the subtle almost seamless understanding of their hearts; <b>language</b> that intensifies every emotion ten times stronger, penetrates and destroys your will to fight the feelings; <b>the story</b> that holds your attention like chess pieces on a board, making you want to guess the rival's next move. <b><i>Everything in this series makes me aglow with life and desire, with longing.</i></b> That's why I love this series. <br /></p><p>From book one to book three <b>main characters came a long way</b> filled with suffering, pain, passion, uncertainty, betrayal and so on. The list of things they endured can go on almost indefinitely. Book one was the beginning, tentative steps to acknowledging characters and the world around. We were mostly isolated and didn't know the stakes of the game everyone around was playing. In book two the world became bigger and the stakes higher. Everyone played everyone and our characters were amateurs in the world of major gamblers. Book three... the stakes are higher still - no saying if you'll survive or the god of death will claim you. <br /></p><p> I think we can <b>divide this book in four acts</b>. <br /><i><u>Act one</u></i> picks up almost from the moment book two ends. <i>Kestrel</i> is on her way to <i>Tundra's</i> working camp, a place where any hope is futile. A place with zero chances to stay the same person you were before you entered it. <b>This is the highest point of Kestrel's suffering.</b> Her former self disappears, dissolves inside a nightmare, and someone new is born. <br /><i><blockquote>It would be a blessing to forget.<br />After all, what was there to remember?<br />Someone she never could have had. Friends dead or gone. A father who did not love her.</blockquote></i><br />Meanwhile <i>Arin</i> prepares for the war with <i>Valoria</i>, and this final battle will determine the future of the whole nations. He feels betrayed, used, abandoned. <b>Isn't it what people do to him all his life: throw him away like an unwanted thing.</b><br /><i><blockquote>No, it didn’t hurt anymore to think about Kestrel. He’d been a fool, but he’d had to forgive himself for worse. Sister, father, mother. As for Kestrel . . . Arin had some clarity on who he was: the sort of person who trusted too blindly, who put his heart where it didn’t belong.</blockquote></i><br />Arin turns to steel, his god protects him and all that left is fighting.<br /><i><blockquote>The man wrote his message.<br />Are you really a boy, like Xash says? the god asked Arin. You’ve been mine for twenty years. I raised you.<br />The Valorian signed the scrap of paper.<br />Cared for you.<br />The message was rolled, sealed, and pushed into a tiny leather tube.<br />Watched over you when you thought you were alone.<br />The captain tied the tube to a hawk’s leg. The bird was too large to be a kestrel. It didn’t have a kestrel’s markings. It cocked its head, turning its glass-bead eyes on Arin.<br />No, not a boy. A man made in my image . . . one who knows he can’t afford to be seen as weak.<br />The hawk launched into the sky.<br />You’re mine, Arin. You know what you must do.<br />Arin cut the Valorian’s throat.</blockquote></i><br /><i><u>Act two</u></i> is about redemption, friendship, hope. <b>Can a damaged person heal another damaged person?</b> Is it possible to find yourself again, to be reborn from the ashes like <i>Phoenix</i>, to find your beacon in a raging storm in the middle of a foaming sea?<br /><i><blockquote>As he spoke, it occurred to her that maybe he, too, felt like two people, that maybe everybody does, and that it’s not a question of whether one’s damaged, but of how easily or not that damage is seen.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>She tried to imagine her former self. Enemy. Prisoner. Friend? Daughter. Spy. Prisoner again. “What am I now?”<br />Sarsine held both of Kestrel’s hands. “Whatever you want to be.”</blockquote><br /><blockquote>Arin thought of Cheat, Tensen, Kestrel. He wondered if some part of him was drawn to lies. What was it that made him so easy to deceive?</blockquote></i><br /><i><u>Act three</u></i> is all about war and revenge. <b> In the end, what would you choose?</b> Revenge or peace? Death or victory? Or are there any other choices? <br /><i><blockquote>The cannons held their breath. Vanguard crashed into vanguard. She saw the collision happen a few ranks ahead. The spurt of blood. Hideous masks of fear and hatred. An arm shorn from the shoulder. Bodies shoved from horses, crumpled into the sand beneath hooves. And the cruelty of what she couldn’t see.</blockquote></i><br />Arin and Kestrel will have to make hard choices and ultimately decide what they are.<br /><i><blockquote>He wondered if he, too, was tempted by cunning. Maybe he was drawn as well to the biggest gamble.<br /></blockquote><br /><blockquote>He hadn’t been blessed by the god of death.<br />Arin was the god.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>It was grief. It was the horror of someone who’d been dealt a winning hand, had bet her life on the game, and then proceeded (deliberately?) to lose.<br /></blockquote><br /><blockquote>Kestrel felt a slow, slight throb, a shimmer in the blood. She knew it well.<br />Her worst trait. Her best trait.<br />The desire to come out on top, to set her opponent under her thumb.<br />A streak of pride. Her mind ringed with hungry rows of foxlike teeth.</blockquote></i><br /><i><u>Act four</u></i> is about absolution. The ultimate game is played, who will live and who will die? <b>Who deserves a second chance?</b><br /><i><blockquote>Kestrel thought that maybe she had been wrong, and Risha had been wrong, about forgiveness, that it was neither mud nor stone, but resembled more the drifting white spores. They came loose from the trees when they were ready. Soft to the touch, but made to be let go, so that they could find a place to plant and grow.</blockquote></i><br /><i><u>Arin &amp; Kestrel</u></i><br /><br /> They <b>hurt each other</b> constantly. Sometimes they don't understand the damage. They are <b>broken</b>, they are <b>lonely</b>. They were <b>made for each other</b>, but the world keeps them apart. <b>Love is not enough when too much power divides you.</b> Did I mention that Arin &amp; Kestrel are my favorite couple in YA? They are. I don't think I've ever read a book about two people so synced, if you hold them together there won't be any visible seams - a perfect match, two halves of one. In this book, they went through hell and more. It literally hurt to read about them, <b><i>I wanted to shout a question to <i>Marie Rutkoski</i>: How did you know how to write them? </i></b> A slow-burning romance - no - it's not just the romance - a partnership, built brick by brick from the ruin of their lives. <br /><i><blockquote>She looked into the shadowed corners of the room. Talking with him was like having a flower unfold inside her chest, then close up tight. Creep open. Collapse in on itself.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>She’d wanted to put her fear inside a white box and give it to Arin. You, too, she would tell him. I fear for you. I fear for me if I lost you.</blockquote></i><br />What they have is hard, it's toxic at times,<br /><i><blockquote>I would do anything for you, she’d written in the letter her father had found. But that part, despite feeling true when she’d scrawled it on the page, had been a lie. Kestrel had refused Arin. She hadn’t been honest with him, not even when he’d begged. She’d pretended she was empty and careless and cruel.<br />He’d believed it. She couldn’t believe that he believed it. Sometimes, she hated him for that.<br /></blockquote></i><br />but at the same time, it's the purest elixir, <b>the essence of love</b>.<br /><i><blockquote>He didn’t smile. He cupped her face with both hands. An emotion tugged at his expression, a dark awe, the kind saved for a wild storm that rends the sky but doesn’t ravage your existence, doesn’t destroy every thing you love. The one that lets you feel saved.<br /></blockquote></i><br /><i><u>Kestrel and her father</u></i><br /><br /><b>Betrayal.</b> This is what between Kestrel and her father. She betrayed him and he betrayed her. But whose act was the ultimate betrayal - an unforgivable crime?<br /><i><blockquote>Harder to know that her father had sent her here. Hard, horrible, the the way he had looked at her, disowned her, accused her of treason. She’d been guilty. She had done every thing that he believed of her, and now she had no father.</blockquote></i><br /><i>General Trojan</i> is a military man, he was raised with certain expectations and code of honor. He tried to raise Kestrel the same way. But when she disagreed with his way, he didn't give her a choice, he put his honor above his daughter. it's a terrible crime.<br /><i><blockquote>But how could he? Why couldn’t he love me most? Or enough. Why couldn’t he love me enough to choose me over his rules?”</blockquote></i><br />Kestrel is hurt beyond words, but this story wouldn't feel realistic if her hatred was absolute. No. <b>Life is complicated. You can love a monster.</b> There's no heroes or villains. There are us and the consequences of our choices that define our future.<br /><i><blockquote>Kestrel hadn’t known until she saw her father’s face how much she still loved him.<br />Wrong, that she felt this way. Wrong, that love could live with betrayal and hurt and anger.<br /></blockquote><br /><blockquote>Her love for him closed within her like a fist. Nervous, bruised. She despised it. Wasn’t it the love of a beaten animal, slinking back to its master? Yet here was the truth: she missed her father.</blockquote></i><br /><i><u>Roshar</u></i><br /><br /> He is the <b>book's light</b>. Sometimes I was overwhelmed by the darkness of the story and <i>Roshar</i> helped me to save a tiny piece of sanity, to look at things from the brighter side. <br /><i><blockquote>Arms folded across his chest, Arin walked to the end of the pier. “Did you have to bring the tiger?”<br />“I kept him hungry during the journey here, just for you,” Roshar said. “Go give him a nice snuggle, won’t you? He’s come all this way to see you. The least you could do is give him one of your arms to eat. Too much? What about a hand? At least some fingers. Arin, where’s your hospitality?”<br /></blockquote><br /><blockquote>“Please understand. When I look at you as if you’re crazy, it’s not that I judge you for your insanity.” </blockquote></i><br />I loved how he mocked Arin and Kestrel. they are so tense most of the time that a little relaxation won't hurt:<br /><i><blockquote>“You could offer her a seat,” Arin said.<br />“Ah, but I have only two chairs in my tent, little Herrani, and we are three. I suppose she could always sit on your lap.”</blockquote></i><br />Of course, Arin decided to stand and Kestrel took the chair. Why ever lose such a great opportunity to rest your legs, Arin?!<br /></p><p>Roshar is not all sunshine and rainbows and often <b>hides his vulnerability behind jokes and self-mockery </b>. He has his sins, he made his stakes, he lost, he continues to live with the guilt. <br /><i><blockquote>“I have a confession,” he said. “Sometimes I offend on purpose. It’s like my smile.”<br />“That’s not an apology.”<br />“Princes don’t apologize.”</blockquote></i><br />His friendship with Arin is something precious, something that lasts forever.<br /><i><blockquote>“How do I look in the dark?”<br />Startled, Arin glanced at him. The question had had no edges. It wasn’t sleek, either. Its soft, uncertain shape suggested that Roshar truly wanted to know. In the fired red shadows, his limbs looked lax and his mutilated face met Arin’s squarely. The heavy feeling that Arin carried—that specific sadness, nestled just below his collar bone, like a pendant—lessened. He said, “Like my friend.”<br />Roshar didn’t smile. When he spoke, his voice matched his expression, which was rare for him. Rarer still: his tone. Quiet and true. “You do, too.”<br /></blockquote></i><br /><i><u>Curious facts:</u> </i><br /><br />- During the writing process Marie Rutkoski listened to: <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HgBtoiNxPyE" rel="nofollow noopener">U2 - bad</a> and <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eMM1lcmgnBQ" rel="nofollow noopener">florence and the machine - take care</a>.<br /><br />- In one of her interviews, Marie mentioned that she may write another fantasy book taking place in <i>The Winner's trilogy</i> world but with different characters. I would like that, the map of the world will widen, maybe we'll learn what's beyond the sea <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>Verex</i> has mentioned at the end of the book that he and <i>Risha</i> would like to travel to new lands. Is that a hint from the author? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I would also like more cunning characters. The strategy is one of my favorite things about this series. It's refreshing to have a heroine who doesn't fight with swords and fists but with her mind. More such heroines in YA would be wonderful.<br /><br />- Did you notice in the acknowledgements of the book how many people helped Marie to create this world, how many different books she read and researched for this fantastic series? I am, as a reader, want to thank Marie and people who helped her create this series. <br /><br /><b><i>************</i></b><br /></p><p>This review has come to an end. Maybe it wasn't a review in its defined form but a map of my emotions and thoughts during my journey through this series. I don't know. I am not sure I can say goodbye to this series yet. I will probably read and re-read it not once, but many times. The thing about favorite books is that they make us stronger even when they make us weaker. Wasn't it what Kestrel said about Arin or Arin said about Kestrel or did they say it about each other? The things we love always hurt us, whether it's books or people or something else. A Bitter-sweet pain that makes us alive.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="10341579848589029377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
