    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_920975667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/920975667" />
    <a title="Andreea Pop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop"><img alt="Andreea Pop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486663526p2/4858513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/920975667?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=gods">gods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=i-worship-these">i-worship-these</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=amazing-feelings">amazing-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=awesome-romance">awesome-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=badass-heroine">badass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=swoon-worthy-characters">swoon-worthy-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920975667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16381676271542633510"><i>
  <b>“Stories will get you killed.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Brilliant. Gods-given, brilliant literature. I am forever in love with these books, because like any other final installment, <i>The Winner's Kiss</i> had the power to shatter the story or to lift it to heavenly skies. And thank the gods, it was beyond beautiful. <b>This</b> is how you end a series. <b>This</b> is how you give readers a satisfying conclusion. And, most importantly, <b>this</b> is how you uphold the promise to your own characters -- you let them come alive. <br/><br/>The previous boo</span>
  <span id="freeText16381676271542633510" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Stories will get you killed.”</b>
</i><br><br>Brilliant. Gods-given, brilliant literature. I am forever in love with these books, because like any other final installment, <i>The Winner's Kiss</i> had the power to shatter the story or to lift it to heavenly skies. And thank the gods, it was beyond beautiful. <b>This</b> is how you end a series. <b>This</b> is how you give readers a satisfying conclusion. And, most importantly, <b>this</b> is how you uphold the promise to your own characters -- you let them come alive. <br><br>The previous book ended on a killer note, one that promised the plot to become even more intricate. Coupled with the fact that lovely Kestrel and dear Arin were broken in their entirety, this serves us sweet agony, tear-jerkers, despair and disbelief in the first quarter of the finale. I might have been emotionally deceased at a couple of scenes. <br><br><a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-dnXQGpZrRHM/Vw1YNJu9XDI/AAAAAAAAP9w/waJ0BxZWaCoxDi7Dg3ZN-MHk16MxgqpawCLcB/s1600/tumblr_lvl5tyId4c1qegw8v.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="169" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460492545ra/18749068.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then the war interweaved with the plot and the bloody dynamics between Valorian and Herrani we've all been expecting finally came into play in a marvelously clever manner worthy of Kestrel's and General Trajan's strategies. Its development had glorious political undertones due to the Dacrans' involvement and it was all so deliciously good. <br><br><a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-5sGkPPiO-14/Vw1YNUMt9BI/AAAAAAAAP90/cMOq62rS7BoZFU31LkI1zedXcJzDEsQrQCLcB/s1600/tumblr_mvi25v29hj1s3h43ko1_r2_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="144" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460492545ra/18749069.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Regarding the writing style, I could see it changed a bit -- such as fractured sentences, rapid successions of short-replies. It blindsided me at the beginning, but as I got used to it, I could realize it actually worked for the book -- the mental state of both narrators was transmitted, the pace felt progressive and my heart was pumping thanks to the tension created. <br><br>Kestrel truly awed me. She has her own parallel journey that brings the whole notion of self-discovery to another level and we see her in a different light, frayed at the edges, but still wonderfully strong, fair, ingenious and compassionate. When you see how far she's come, how she pulled herself up from ruins, you instantly feel a sense of pride because Kestrel Trajan is the ultimate badass heroine -- one that fights with her brains, not with her swords. Her emotional specter puts her as a central piece in the chessboard of war and her legacy and mind forever changes the fate of the ill-fated Herrani. <br><br><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-nW9jrPLle54/Vw1XLT4Ai6I/AAAAAAAAP9g/AItBA7taWggkN6xpgoCNL-xrDHnS4aruwCLcB/s1600/kestrel.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460492126i/18748992.jpg" width="239" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“You talk about her as if she’s made of spun glass. Know what I see? Steel.”</b>
</i><br><br>Arin, on the other hand, I was mad at in the beginning. He was quick to bury Kestrel at the bottom of his thoughts and that just gutted me considering how Kestrel was fairing in that particular moment. The double narrative built a thrilling crescendo for their dramatic -- and imperative -- reunion, but that did not lessen the fact I was internally happy about the remorse, guilt, self-hate Arin felt. His character-development is rather interesting, with a drop of Herrani myths woven into his persona, one that nuanced him as an ambitious, loved and courageous leader. However, the dynamics between him and Kestrel also painted him as a sick love-puppy and let's be honest, we all appreciate his romantic and swoon-worthy side. In one word, he is dreamy. <br><br><a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-I8HAYglHEE0/Vw1XMIW1hYI/AAAAAAAAP9k/tqcq_tmwJwA08cJD6cOCxpbLqgAzQOclACLcB/s1600/Arin.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460492126i/18748993.jpg" width="224" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Other remarkable characters developed wonderfully. Roshar, for instance, was amazing. Humorous, strategic, loyal, the know it all type we all love in secondary cast. The bromance between him and Arin was gloriously happiness-inducing. And most of his lines offered the comical relief for the dramatic tension; I honestly laughed out loud countless times. He truly was the icing on the cake. <br><br>Moreover, Risha brought an interesting spin on the story. Sarsine was great as always, Verex cute and lovable and the Emperor still a megalomaniac. Shocker, right? I especially liked the closure of Trajan's storyline, it seemed fitting to end it sort of halfway, to get revenge but still forgive. It illustrates how no matter what we try to tell ourselves, we'll always protect the people we love no matter how much they've hurt us. <br><br><a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-mzZk4mwgDnA/Vw1Y6nGOiCI/AAAAAAAAP98/xlU5_iUSbQgA7MBZuAefx_oHcKnylOZWwCLcB/s1600/tumblr_inline_nsjnp2wRG81raozs1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="179" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460492545ra/18749070.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“Sometimes a truth squeezes you so tightly you can’t breathe.”</b>
</i><br><br>Without a doubt, TWK is now one of my all time favorites and certainly one of my favorite finales, right there along with <i>Clockwork Princess</i> by Cassie Clare, <i>Champion</i> by Marie Lu and <i>The Forever Song</i> by Julie Kagawa. I am sad we won't have more of Kestrel &amp; Arin or more Roshar, but the joy I'm feeling now far outweighs any bitter remnants of literary desire. <br><br><i>The Winner's Kiss</i> is enchanting, romantic and masterfully told, a book that grips your heart and soul. Kestrel and Arin truly became the power couple I deemed them to be and they shine brightly. So much love for this series, this author and these characters. Go read it. Doesn't matter you just did -- you'll thank yourself for a re-read. <br><br><i>
  <b>“I want better choices.”<br>“Then we must make a world that has them.”</b>
</i><br><br><b>ENJOY! &lt;3</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16381676271542633510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0y0BvKCj0RKrV6KJUsJnb+giMwTkSRe3irGR+zazYREwwprmKC/6AGkktFVAX6F8M1oBbDukcrmAHeNkByjceQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GF66fFu3yhWsWmZmWl0Cs9ji7KQCsyO9k6G22X4tpt/7sSEm0zvhB24pcLpIwMSgA5rezN1eRrOZDcRGT7Ybtw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7864800770424150351">Marie Rutkoski is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of The Winner's Trilogy, which begins with <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. She also wrote the YA novel <i>The Shadow Society</i> and the children's fantasy series The Kronos Chronicles, including <i>The Cabinet of Wonders</i>. Her next project is a YA duology set in the same world as <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. The first in this duology is called <i>The Midnight Lie</i> and will be </span>
  <span id="freeText7864800770424150351" style="display:none">Marie Rutkoski is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of The Winner's Trilogy, which begins with <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. She also wrote the YA novel <i>The Shadow Society</i> and the children's fantasy series The Kronos Chronicles, including <i>The Cabinet of Wonders</i>. Her next project is a YA duology set in the same world as <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. The first in this duology is called <i>The Midnight Lie</i> and will be published in March 2020. <br /><br />Marie grew up in Bolingbrook, Illinois (a suburb of Chicago), as the oldest of four children. She holds a BA from the University of Iowa and a PhD from Harvard University. Marie is currently a professor at Brooklyn College, where she teaches Renaissance Drama, children's literature and fiction writing. She lives in Brooklyn with her two sons.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/marierutkoski">http://us.macmillan.com/author/marier...</a></span>
